Current Commentary

Japan Further Expands Military Budget 31

Since the establishment of the Okada Cabinet in Japan, it has increasingly estimated the so-called international crisis of 1935-1936 and heightened its sense of national defense security, placing emphasis on naval armaments to strive for absolute superiority on the Pacific Ocean. Therefore, in the next year's naval budget, it will focus on (1) completing the first naval replenishment plan and increasing maintenance costs for new ships; (2) forming new air squadrons and their maintenance costs; (3) renovating old ships; (4) building new ships. These types of budgets are estimated at 275 million Japanese yen. Adding the already determined expenditure of 420 million yen and 19 million yen for increased costs due to rising prices, the total naval budget will reach 714 million yen. On the army side, there are new demands for air defense enhancement expenses, military equipment improvement expenses, and Manchurian incident expenses, totaling no less than 320 million yen. Adding the already determined expenditure of 230 million yen, the total amounts to approximately 550 million yen. The combined total for the army and navy is 1.264 billion yen, which is 328 million yen more than this year's military expenditure of 936 million yen. This truly marks the entry into a wartime budget period.

Japanese militarists are obsessed with the ambition of dominating the Pacific. They also believe that the development of Japan's overseas trade and the opening of markets must rely on the absolute superiority of the navy to maintain future security and ensure the smooth flow of exports. Therefore, at the beginning of Okada's rise to power, army and navy personnel vigorously advocated the high-sounding principle of national defense security, which Okada then supported, prioritizing the strengthening of the navy. Consequently, they disregarded everything and exerted all their strength to develop their military operational strengths, such as increasing the construction of submarines, enhancing light and heavy cruisers, and increasing air squadrons, all with the aim of expanding defenses in the Pacific Ocean. In other words, they are implementing their so-called Asian Monroe Doctrine. Although the army has not immediately increased new divisions, the number of troops stationed in various parts of the Northeast exceeds 100,000. The 3rd, 7th, 10th, 11th, and 16th divisions, and other special units within Japan, have all become expeditionary forces stationed for extended periods in various parts of the Northeast. In their original garrison areas, equivalent reserve units have been conscripted. Therefore, the Japanese army has increased its regular army strength by at least about 100,000. As for the army's efforts to enhance its air squadrons, the goal is to completely replace old-style aircraft and extend their range to 12,000 kilometers. Thus, the Japanese air force can threaten Vladivostok, travel between Hong Kong and Tokorozawa, and have more than enough capability to threaten the Philippines. With such significant progress, who can doubt their intention to launch a war?

Therefore, besides Russia, the country that feels most endangered by Japan's expansion of armaments is the United States, which is far away on the other side of the Pacific. In peacetime, the United States is wary of the difficulties facing naval disarmament conferences, fearing that once the principle of proportionality is broken, the balance of power in the Far East will not be maintained, and future market expansion will be obstructed. Considering the existing naval strength, Japan's submarines and cruisers are already superior to those of the United States. The only areas where it lags behind are battleships and air squadrons. Japan, taking advantage of this natural geographic advantage in the Western Pacific, even without huge battleships, is already more than capable of seizing the Philippines and capturing Guam. If it forms a strong air force, there is concern that the Aleutian Islands will also have difficulty accommodating the stable presence of the U.S. Air Force. Previously, when Japan advocated for naval parity and the abolition of the Washington and London treaties, the United States strongly advocated for peace, believing that the principle of proportionality should not be changed abruptly and further proposed reducing existing forces by 20 percent. However, Japan is expanding its forces as much as possible and is now unprecedentedly increasing its military budget. Although the United States is extremely cautious in this situation, can it not fear the damage to its interests in the Far East and consider timely precautions? Recently, the United States has paid great attention to armaments, seeking to maintain its forward base in Hawaii and build up its air defenses in Alaska, all of which have been prompted by Japan's intensified military expansion plans.

England is already in an economically irreconcilable position with Japan. Now, seeing Japan's steady progress in expanding its military strength, which subjects the Far Eastern market entirely to the control of Japanese power, even the security of areas as far west as India is threatened. Australia, located in the remote South Pacific, must also increase its defenses. Consequently, England is also catching up urgently, and the relationship between England and Japan is becoming increasingly divided. In short, the result of Japan's increased military spending is merely to stir up war clouds over the Pacific.

Seeking Peace in the Pacific

Conclusion of a Six-Nation Pact 32

Proposed by Soviet Russia, Opposed by Japan

Attitudes of the U.S., Britain, and France Appear Cold

(London) Recently, there has been discussion about forming a six-nation pact to maintain peace in the Pacific, based on the Eastern European Locarno Pact. The so-called six nations are Britain, the United States, Japan, Russia, China, and France. The core of this plan is to unite the naval and military forces of the six nations to assist countries that are invaded to resist foreign aggression. Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov made a similar proposal to U.S. disarmament representative Davis between May and June of this year. At that time, Davis only listened to it without making any criticism or indicating any opinions from Washington. Last winter, when Litvinov visited President Roosevelt in the United States, he seemed to have this plan in mind, but the initial proposal only included China, the United States, and Russia. Even after discussions by the White House or the State Department, no results were achieved. Later, between March and May of this year, it was reported that the Japanese ambassador to the United States, Saito, had also proposed that Japan and the United States sign a non-aggression treaty, but it was abandoned due to a lack of support from the United States. Currently, the forces for and against the Pan-Pacific Security Pact are becoming more distinct. Moscow strongly supports it because, after the pact is established, if Japan attacks Soviet Russia, other countries can provide assistance. Japan strongly opposes it because this type of plan is tantamount to encircling Japan, leaving it no room for expansion in the Far East. China is also said to have expressed sympathy for this proposal because it can prevent further Japanese aggression. France is equivocal, not wanting to offend Japan and risk conflicts between French interests in French Indochina and Yunnan Province with Japan, nor willing to reject its Soviet ally. Britain is quite cold, fearing it would harm Anglo-Japanese relations. The most important factor is the attitude of the United States. According to current information, Washington believes that this plan is not yet timely. The United States is currently withdrawing its naval and military forces from the eastern Pacific. President Roosevelt is determined to achieve Philippine independence. Observers believe that only one thing can expedite the withdrawal of U.S. troops from the Philippines: the conclusion of a treaty between Japan and the United States, with Britain participating, guaranteeing the independence of the Philippines, similar to Britain's pre-war guarantee of Belgian independence. The United States is currently trying to befriend Japan in order to achieve the goal of Philippine neutrality. Therefore, it is unwilling to discuss a Pan-Pacific Security Treaty that may conflict with Japan and prevent the Philippine neutrality plan from succeeding. Therefore, discussions on the treaty are becoming increasingly inactive. (12th National Telegram)

Japan Exerts All Efforts

To Address Naval Preparatory Meeting 33

Plans to Increase Dispatch of Diplomatic Representatives

To Assist Political Negotiations

(Nanjing) For the disarmament preliminary talks reopening in October, the Navy has dispatched Colonels Masasuke Shimomura and Yasutaro Iwashita to London. Rear Admiral Isoroku Yamamoto, who was previously scheduled to be dispatched, is also scheduled to depart for London in late August. Naval Attaché Colonel Oka Shin, stationed at the Japanese Embassy in Britain, has also decided to participate in the talks. The Navy's lineup is already so complete. Although the talks in October will focus on specialized technical issues, there will inevitably be political negotiations alongside them. Foreign Minister Hirota, in view of this, plans to send diplomats familiar with internal and external affairs to London to assist Ambassador Matsudaira in conducting the negotiations. Hirota will soon propose this matter to Navy Minister Osumi, and it is expected that Osumi will have no objection. (12th China United Press Telegram)

Mechanization of the British Army 34

(London) The "People's Daily" reports that the British Army is about to undergo a major reform, the significance of which is unprecedented since the Battle of Waterloo. "In the future, an infantry brigade will have one 'heavy battalion' and three 'light battalions.' Each 'heavy battalion' will be equipped with heavy machine guns and trench mortars. Each 'light battalion' soldier will be equipped with new automatic rifles and small-caliber machine guns for individual use. In addition, the 'Royal Artillery' will be completely mechanized and equipped with 3.7-inch light guns. As for the shovels and other tools used by the engineers, they will be replaced by machines, such as rubber-tired plows and gasoline-powered machine shovels used for road construction. Moreover, the excavation of trenches or the construction of protective works for the artillery, which previously required a week to complete with old tools, can now be completed within an hour using new machines," it said. (12th Havas Telegram)

To Make Up for Budget Shortfall

Japanese Military Proposes Tax Increase 36

Reasons for Opposition from the Ministry of Finance

(Tokyo) The military is demanding that the Ministry of Finance increase taxes from next year to serve as emergency preparedness expenses. It is currently watching what financial plan Finance Minister Fujii has regarding the formulation of next year's budget. This is because the market is quite developed now. Although rural areas are said to be exhausted, it is only a small part. This opportunity should be taken to properly handle the accumulated deficit bonds, promptly correct the financial plan, and establish a permanent financial structure. Therefore, it seems that consideration should be given to increasing tax rates on the wealthy class. However, merely increasing taxes on the wealthy class will provide only a small amount of financial resources. A tax for emergency periods should also be added to military-related industries, but this method will also result in very little government income and may hinder the development of military-related industries that are in the process of development. Therefore, the tax increase implemented to supplement financial resources should be on transportation taxes, postal taxes, and other taxes collected from the entire nation. Otherwise, it will be difficult to achieve the goal. Therefore, the military side advocates reforming the entire tax system as a key plan. (12th Japan United Press Telegram)

(Nanjing) Before the budget for next year is compiled, the military and a part of the House of Peers are advocating for the implementation of tax increases. However, the Ministry of Finance, based on the following viewpoints, believes that it is not yet the time to implement tax increases: (1) Before the crisis of 1935-1936, defense spending and expenditures are expanding, and their future is difficult to predict. Therefore, tax increases cannot be implemented if there is hope for a considerable reduction in expenditures. (2) Judging from the state of the economy, although the future is bright, the overall surplus of national power has not yet been reached. Therefore, setting up a tax increase now will result in the destruction of the budding industries that are developing and thriving, which would be undermining the morale of the people. (3) Even if the so-called emergency income tax is implemented, the amount of income tax obtained will be very small and cannot serve as a powerful source of revenue to replace public bonds. (4) Although a gradual tax increase is necessary, the tax system involves local taxes, so it is necessary to consider the overall situation and conduct a thorough investigation to reduce the burden on rural areas before it can be implemented. (12th Electric Communication Society Telegram)

Sharp Increase in Japanese Tenant Farmer Disputes

Reflecting Rural Exhaustion 37

According to an investigation by the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry reported by the China United Press Tokyo dispatch, there were 2,594 disputes between landlords and tenant farmers between January and July 10 of this year, an increase of 387 cases compared to the previous year, which is the highest record in recent years. The content of the disputes all reflects the true state of exhaustion of the farmers. That is, 70% of the dispute cases are disputes arising because tenant farmers cannot pay rent, and landlords want to take back their land. Among the dispute cases, 1,670 cases have been resolved, and 920 cases remain unresolved. Among the parties to the disputes, there are 6,106 landlords and 19,420 tenant farmers.

Soviet Russian Government Bulletin

Exposing Japanese Provocative Actions 51

Japanese Puppet Regime Intensifies Malicious Propaganda

Attempting to Seize the Chinese Eastern Railway by Force

Hirota Abandons Mediation, Negotiations for Purchase Near Collapse

(Moscow) A paper titled "A Naive and Harmful Game" was published in the Soviet government bulletin, stating, "Recently, Japanese and Manchukuo newspapers, following a set goal, have begun a new anti-Soviet movement, attempting to create new conflicts between the Soviet Union and Japan through violent attacks, barbaric anti-Soviet rumors, and other naive methods." The paper dismissed the Japanese and Manchukuo's false claims that the Soviet Red Army crossed the border and that Soviet planes flew over Manchukuo territory, and emphasized that the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway conference is the main factor determining the current Soviet-Japanese relations. The paper continued to comment, "The anti-Soviet movement of Japanese and Manchukuo newspapers is consistent with the new and rude provocations of the Japanese and Manchukuo government authorities. The arrest of Soviet people and illegal searches of Soviet institutions have also reappeared on the Chinese Eastern Railway. In other words, an interesting game has begun, attempting to incite incidents in the eastern border of the Soviet Union. This extremely rude anti-Soviet movement has already exceeded the scope of 'Manchukuo' and the Manchurian question. The [unclear transliteration] newspaper has widely spread this crude story, claiming that the Soviet Union has completed aircraft and chemical bases in Kulun." Japanese newspapers are maliciously distorting the Soviet Union's peaceful policy, and creating a new argument, saying that the Soviet Union's globally recognized peaceful policy, especially its efforts to complete the Eastern Peace Treaty, is aimed at attacking Japan. The Soviet government bulletin interpreted this as, "The purpose of this new argument is clearly to deceive the Japanese people, but they are already deeply aware of the Soviet Union's peaceful policy and can judge it based on the merits of this policy. No one in Europe and America will listen to such a distortion of the Soviet Union's foreign policy. The current anti-Soviet movement of Japanese and Manchukuo newspapers is directly related to the Chinese Eastern Railway conference, and is used as a naive means of threatening the Soviet Union." The bulletin also emphasized that the Soviet Union has proposed selling the Chinese Eastern Railway as a way to ease the situation in the Far East, pointing out that the Japanese side wants to buy the Chinese Eastern Railway at a paltry price, which is no different from trying to seize the railway freely. They do not hesitate to use means to achieve this goal, such as various provocations on the Chinese Eastern Railway during key periods of the Tokyo conference, threatening the Soviet Union, which is one of the means. The bulletin further stated, "The instigators of the anti-Soviet movement must remember that the extremists among them, especially those active in Manchuria, will use this movement to prepare for war." Tanaka, in the "[unclear transliteration]" newspaper in Harbin, said, "If war breaks out, the Chinese Eastern Railway problem will be easily solved." The Soviet government bulletin commented on this, "Tanaka's words are undoubtedly extremely wrong. He uses this extremely difficult and dangerous method as an easy solution. The Japanese and Manchukuo sides, in order to obtain a cheap bargain of several million yen, do not hesitate to plunge the relationship between the two countries into a dangerous situation. This situation has already formed, and this is the basis of the problem. The most barbaric and dangerous anti-Soviet movement expressed in Japanese and Manchukuo newspapers is due to this internal cause. The Soviet Union has shown the greatest goodwill in the Tokyo conference, far more than the Japanese side. If the conference is unsuccessful, it is entirely due to the tactics adopted by the Japanese and Manchukuo sides. The leaders who instigated the attack on the Soviet Union and the unreasonable threat to the Soviet Union must recognize the game they are playing. The whole world understands this as well as the Soviet Union. They will eventually know that completing the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway can only be achieved through free trade between the two parties. Any party that wants to use coercion will not be effective. Japanese politicians who think intelligently should take the opportunity to realize that the newspaper movement cannot control the Tokyo conference, nor can it support their unreasonable claims with naive and harmful provocative actions. The key to the successful outcome of the conference is the sincerity of both parties."

The editor of Pravda also commented as follows, "We are facing a new attempt by the Japanese rulers. They want to threaten the progress of the Chinese Eastern Railway sale conference through various barbaric acts." According to the report of Mr. Rutai, director of the Chinese Eastern Railway Bureau, the Japanese and Manchukuo sides continue to destroy the railway, and the effort they spend is more than that of the Tokyo conference. The newspaper continued, "The Japanese side uses the real power in Manchuria, which is entirely in their hands, to do its best to destroy the Chinese Eastern Railway, and on the other hand, uses newspapers to create public opinion for forcibly seizing the railway. The provocative methods of the Japanese imperialists to seize the Chinese Eastern Railway have already aroused the anger of the Soviet workers. They have sufficient reason to conclude that the unreasonable anti-Soviet movement of Japanese and Manchukuo newspapers is a preparatory means for attacking the Soviet Union. However, we must warn the instigators of this movement that their provocative attempts will suffer a shameful defeat, no different from the previous attempts. The Japanese rulers will gain nothing from fraud and threats. All that they hope for in this is an empty bubble." (TASS dispatch, 11th)

US Silver Acquisition as National Property

Tendency Towards Expansionary Policies 57

Will Issue 80 Million Yuan in Silver Certificates

(Washington) The expansionist faction in Congress and the semi-official government today launched a movement to further devalue the US dollar through the power of the silver nationalization plan in order to achieve expansionist goals. The procedure is roughly as follows: first, further devalue the US dollar; second, the Treasury Department will issue more paper money; third, the President will appoint a committee to deal with this issue and suggest what the value of the US dollar should be, and plan to use silver as much as possible under the nationalization order. The Treasury Department today officially announced that the government only intends to issue silver certificates based on the legal price of 1.29 yuan per dollar based on the silver currently held by the Treasury Department. The silver received under the current nationalization order will be temporarily issued with paper money at a purchase price of 50.1 cents per ounce. There are currently 62 million taels of silver stored in the national treasury, so the significance is that silver certificates worth 80 million yuan will be issued. According to this move, it is also a low-level expansionary policy, because the government only spent 46.9 million yuan to purchase this silver. According to the authorities, the difference is the profit from minting coins. Some observers believe that President Roosevelt and Treasury Secretary Morgenthau disagree on expansionary policies. Treasury officials have tried their best to deny this. Observers said that Roosevelt ordered on July 17 to issue 80 million yuan in silver certificates with silver stored in the national treasury, while the Treasury Secretary often said that the amount issued should be 46.9 million yuan, which is equal to the value of the silver in storage. Although the President and the Treasury Secretary both advocate that the silver price should be 1.29 yuan per ounce, there seems to be a discrepancy in the amount to be issued. This matter has nothing to do with the silver received under the nationalization order. In addition to the 200 million ounces received by the government under the nationalization order, it must purchase another 130 million ounces to be sufficient to form a ratio of three to one with the gold in storage. The Treasury Department further stated that the silver received this time will be used as government assets. Today, the Treasury Department spoke with the press to explain the silver nationalization plan. Some people believe that this speech was intended to eliminate the rumors of expansion. Treasury officials answered questions raised by the press, saying that all silver in the national treasury will be issued in silver coins at a value of 1.29 yuan per ounce. The silver currently received is like purchasing 1 million ounces at 50.16 cents per ounce, which will cost 516,000 yuan. If the government issues 516,000 yuan in silver certificates at the legal silver price, it will require 400,000 ounces of silver. The remaining 600,000 ounces will be stored in the national treasury as government assets. (National Telegram, 11th)

The waves surged and subsided, rising and falling by thirty feet, attacking the coast for several miles. The locals all believe that it is something they have not seen in decades. Various Factions Rise to Seize Power

The Ugaki Faction Actively Seeks to Form a Cabinet

Using the extraordinary situation as a shield and Prime Minister Okada as a puppet, they maintained good relations with the military, intending to dissolve the Diet and hold new elections to establish new forces in the parliament, so they could dominate the future situation. However, this plan only succeeded partially. Unexpectedly, internal rifts arose due to personnel relations, leading to a confrontational situation. Former Chief Secretary Horikiri, former Police Chief Matsumoto, Police Superintendent-General Fujinuma, and former Chief Secretary Shibata, etc., were greatly dissatisfied. Fujinuma only agreed to stay after repeated persuasion from Interior Minister Goto. Among the parliamentarians who have joined the club, there are thirteen members of the Seiyukai and twelve members of the Minseito. However, the Suzuki faction believes that this organization is detrimental to the overall situation, so they are secretly planning to proceed. It is said that Kabayama Sukehide of the Satsuma faction and Adachi Nakano, who is from Kyushu, will also be included. On the other hand, the Governor-General of Korea, Ugaki, also intends to take the opportunity to resign in preparation for engaging in central political activities after his resignation. He also hopes for the dissolution of the Diet and the formation of a new party. It is rumored that he has prepared an election fund of ten million yuan. This huge sum of money was provided by Kansai Zaibatsu, Katsutaro Inahata, Abe Fusajiro, and Masatsune Ogura, etc., and the Katakura Group. The plan for the new party includes the Minseito, the Kokumin Domei, the Tokonami faction, and also has the understanding of the Research Association of the House of Peers and the Koheikai. In the future general election, they want to shatter the Seiyukai's signboard in one fell swoop, gain a majority of seats in the House of Representatives, elect General Ugaki as the party leader, take over the new regime after the Okada transitional cabinet, and undertake the crisis of 1935-1936 with a grand national unity party, realizing the Ugaki Cabinet.

The Upper Reaches of the Yellow River Rise Sharply 86

A Rise of 2.8 Meters Within Twenty Hours

The River Affairs Bureau Telegraphs an Order for Strict Alert Throughout the Entire River

Han Orders County Magistrates Along the River to Reside on the Levees

Jinan Communication: Although the Yellow River's water level increased due to the continuous rain in various provinces last month, it quickly receded. Unexpectedly, the upper reaches have suddenly and violently risen again in recent days. Yesterday morning, the River Affairs Bureau received a telegram from the Yellow River Conservancy Commission stating, "According to the Tongguan telegram, there was a continued rise of 90 centimeters on the ninth. At 8 PM, the water level was 322.95 meters, and the flow rate was 6,960 cubic meters." According to a telegram from the Shaanxi Prefecture Water Level Station at 1:15 AM on the tenth, "At noon on the ninth, the water level was 294.02 meters, an increase of 1.73 meters from the previous level, and the flow rate was 6,500 cubic meters." Based on this, the River Affairs Bureau immediately telegraphed orders to county magistrates along the river and all chief and sub-section chiefs, etc., to take strict precautions. After sending the telegrams, another urgent telegram was received from Shaanxi Prefecture stating, "At 8 AM on the tenth, the water level there was 295.13 meters, an increase of 1.11 meters from noon on the ninth, and the flow rate also increased to 8,000 cubic meters." It is estimated that from noon on the ninth to the morning of the tenth, within twenty hours, the river water in Shaanxi County rose sharply by 2.84 meters. The speed of the increase is alarming. The raging torrents are rushing downstream. It is estimated that they will reach Shandong province by the morning of the twelfth. River Affairs Bureau Director Zhang Lianjia telegraphed Chairman Han and the Civil Affairs and Construction Departments and re-telegraphed to the county magistrates of each county and the chief and sub-section chiefs of the entire river, urging them to take precautions day and night and not to be negligent. Due to the urgency of the situation, the River Affairs Bureau is also working day and night, sending telegrams at any time to instruct matters to avoid accidents. The River Affairs Bureau telegraphed to Chairman Han, "To the esteemed Chairman Han Jun of the Shandong Provincial Government in Qingdao: We have investigated that the river water in this province has been rising continuously in recent days, and many sections have already reached full capacity. We were taking precautions when we received a telegram from the Shaanxi Prefecture Hydrological Station stating that there was a sharp rise of 2.84 meters from noon to the morning. It is estimated that it will reach Shandong province early in the morning. The water is vast, and the work situation is tight. In addition to ordering all sections to take proper precautions day and night and separately telegraphing to the county magistrates of each county along the river to assist at any time to avoid negligence, we respectfully report. River Affairs Bureau Director Zhang Lianjia kowtows in respect." After receiving the telegram, Han immediately telegraphed Secretary-General Zhang Shaotang of the Provincial Government, separately telegraphing to the county magistrates of twenty-two counties along the river: Heze, Puyang, Fanxian, Shouzhang, Yanggu, Yuncheng, Juan Cheng, Dong'a, Pingyin, Feicheng, Licheng, Qihe, Changqing, Zhangqiu, Jiyang, Qidong Huimin, Qingcheng, Putai, Dongping, Lijin, Binzhou, etc., ordering them to move to the levees by a deadline to supervise the work and rescue. Civil Affairs Department Head Li Shuchun also sent the same telegram last night to the counties along the river, ordering them to move to the levees to supervise the work.

As for the Yellow River water level, according to a telegram from Shaanxi County, at 8 PM on the tenth, the water level dropped by 10 centimeters, the water level was 295.03 meters, and the flow rate was around 8,000 cubic meters. The water level is still very vast and turbulent. Jinan Mayor Wen Cheng

Page 10

He strongly believed that Luokou protected Jinan. The lives and property of 400,000 Chinese and foreign residents were of great importance. Yesterday, he went to inspect the upper and lower sections of Luokou in the rain. He returned that evening and immediately prepared for rescue works. This morning (the eleventh) at about 8:00 AM, he convened a meeting in the city government with Wei Echen, the Director of the Public Security Bureau of the Northeast Township, and the heads of various towns in Luokou to discuss matters related to river defense. It is reported that it has been decided to build more sheds along the coast of Luokou to facilitate day and night defense and ensure safety, and rescue materials will be transported to the construction site by trucks. More than 20 engineers will be dispatched to assist the work, and Liu Hongxiang, a city government staff member, will be sent to guide and supervise and report at any time. The Luokou rescue worksite extends from Yangzhuang in the west to Gajia Gou in the east. It will be fully deployed tonight. It is reported that he will also personally supervise tomorrow (the twelfth).

Today, the upper reaches of the Yellow River in the province rose slightly, while the middle and lower reaches remained stable. The water levels are as follows: Li Sheng Tun water level: 58.12 meters, up 2.9 centimeters; Guanzhuang water level: 35.031 meters, up 0.3 centimeters; Luokou water level: 29.45 meters, down 0.6 centimeters; Xiezhiwan water level: 18.47 meters, down 2 centimeters; Dama Jia water level: 14 meters, down 3 centimeters.

Also, in Dongping County, there are no official dikes for river defense, only a small embankment about thirty miles long. A few days ago, due to the rising river water, the civilian embankment in Shentun was thin and had collapsed in places. Dongping County Magistrate Zhang Zhixi believed that if there was any negligence in this area, Dong'a, Pingyin, and Shouzhang counties would be the first to be affected. He telegraphed the provincial government, requesting approval to use the county's Third Section local public funds for rescue protection. The Ministry of Finance was instructed to jointly review the request with the River Affairs Bureau. Later, the Ministry of Finance joined the review. While the review was in progress, the county magistrate telegraphed again, stating that the work situation was urgent and requesting approval to transfer funds from the Huaqiao donations stored locally for warehouse use to meet the urgent needs. Dong Nianzhou, section chief of the Ministry of Civil Affairs, and Du Zhaotian, director of the River Affairs Bureau, discussed this matter in the Ministry of Civil Affairs today and decided to reply to the county, approving the allocation of 5,000 yuan from the donations of overseas Chinese for application. A letter was sent to the Ministry of Finance, and a report was submitted to the Provincial Government for record. (The Eleventh)

Regulations for the Custody of the Eastern Tombs 87

Thirteen Articles Formulated by the Hebei Provincial Government

Tianjin Communication: When Malanyu is received, the Eastern Tombs will be placed in our custody. The general outline has been detailed in previous letters. The regulations of the Custody Committee have been found and are recorded as follows: Article 1. The Hebei Provincial Government, in order to take care of the Eastern Tombs, mausoleums, historical sites, buildings, sacrificial vessels, and all items, has established the Eastern Tombs Mausoleums and Historical Sites Custody Committee. Article 2. The Eastern Tombs Mausoleums and Historical Sites Custody Committee shall have seven members, including representatives of the Department of Civil Affairs, representatives of the Department of Industry, the Commissioner of the Jibei Administrative Inspectorate, the Magistrate of Xinglong County, the Director of the Malanyu Office of the Commissioner's Office, and two representatives of the Qing Imperial Family in Beiping. The Administrative Inspectorate Commissioner shall serve as the representative. Article 3. The members and chairman of the committee (excluding the Qing Imperial Family representative) shall be appointed by the provincial government. The Beiping Qing Imperial Family representative shall be appointed by the provincial government after the chairman consults with the Beiping Qing Imperial Family. The term of office is two years. Article 4. The Eastern Tombs Mausoleums and Historical Sites Custody Committee may, as necessary for its duties, establish a number of technicians, clerks, and secretaries, all of whom shall be appointed by the committee and reported to the provincial government for record. Article 5. Except for the Beiping Qing Imperial Family representative, technicians, clerks, and secretaries, all other members shall not receive salaries. Article 6. The Eastern Tombs base area shall be limited to the boundary of the mausoleum base area designated by the provincial government. Article 7. The land under the custody of the Eastern Tombs Mausoleums and Historical Sites Custody Committee shall be the land of the mausoleum base, sacrificial land, and the land of the Yongji Preparatory Warehouses. Article 8. The land rent mentioned above shall be used for the committee's expenses, all security, and construction purposes. The land rent to be paid by each county shall be strictly assessed by the Department of Finance and ordered to be collected. Article 9. Repairs of Eastern Tombs destruction, replanting of trees, protection against theft and excavation, and various new construction projects shall be handled by the committee. The required expenses shall be drawn from the land rent, but a plan shall be drafted in advance and submitted to the provincial government for approval before it can be handled. In addition, the Eastern Tombs worship expenses shall be determined by the committee in the revenue item and allocated to the Qing Imperial Family on an annual basis for their own handling. Article 10. A number of police officers shall be stationed at the Eastern Tombs for patrol. Article 11. The Eastern Tombs Mausoleums and Historical Sites Custody Committee's operating expenses budget shall be determined by the committee and submitted to the provincial government for approval and implementation. Article 12. The detailed rules for the Eastern Tombs Mausoleums and Historical Sites Custody Committee shall be determined separately. Article 13. These measures shall take effect from the date of promulgation. (The Tenth)

The Government of the Dutch East Indies Restricts Porcelain Imports 88

Japanese Delegation Lodges a Serious Protest

The Future of the Meeting is Likely to Fall into a Stalemate

Batavia Special Dispatch: The economic control implemented by the Dutch government on the Dutch East Indies due to the dumping of Japanese goods, and the subsequent promulgation of foreign goods import restriction laws, have severely impacted Japanese goods. The Japanese side has been forced to request a one-day Dutch-Japanese meeting, hoping to ease the Dutch attitude towards Japan. However, since the opening of the meeting, nearly two months have passed. Although there was once a slight development in the middle due to the discussion of expert review, it soon returned to obscurity. There is still no slightest approach between the two sides' opinions. However, one more thing has happened recently that is worthy of our attention, that is, after the Dutch East Indies government's implementation of the cotton fabric import restriction law, it suddenly announced a three-month restriction on porcelain imports. After this news was released, the Japanese side was greatly shocked, because the Japanese goods occupy a large part of the Dutch East Indies' porcelain market. If this law is implemented, it is equivalent to giving Japan another extremely large blow. Therefore, the Japanese delegation attending the Dutch-Japanese meeting, upon learning of this, the chief representative Nagaoka immediately lodged a strong protest to the Dutch East Indies government.

The main idea of the Japanese protest letter is roughly: "There is a prior agreement between the Japanese and Dutch governments that the implementation of the Dutch East Indies' restriction law on 56 kinds of commodities must be postponed during the Dutch-Japanese meeting. This time, the Dutch side suddenly issued a porcelain import restriction order without any prior statement, violating the above-mentioned agreement. This fact violates international practice, and its reasons are extremely illegal. If this is the case, it is no longer known whether the Dutch side has the sincerity to continue the meeting. Based on friendly relations, but taking such measures in the meeting, it is really intolerable in terms of normal internationalism concepts and etiquette. Hereafter, it is hoped that the Dutch East Indies side will make every effort to seek understanding." From the wording of the above protest, we can see the strong attitude of the Japanese side. If the Dutch side does not give way, it is really difficult to predict whether the Dutch-Japanese meeting can continue to be held in the future.

According to a Tokyo dispatch on July 26, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs expressed its opinion in the form of a talk regarding the Dutch East Indies government's issuance of a restriction on the import of ceramics, saying that once the official report is received and the situation is clarified, the Japanese government will demand the Dutch side's reflection, and a decision has already been made regarding appropriate measures for the aftermath. However, it is unknown whether the so-called "determination of appropriate measures" of the Japanese government is only a kind of false intimidation or whether there is really a so-called method. However, judging from the general trend, Dutch East Indies-Japanese merchants have no choice but to make passive transportation shutdowns. As for the Japanese authorities being willing to bet on the breakdown of the meeting, it seems to be an expected thing.

As for the Dutch East Indies government's sudden announcement of a porcelain import restriction order this time, although it has a demonstrative nature towards Japan, its inside story is not without cause. According to news from the Dutch East Indies Economic Department, not long ago, fourteen Japanese porcelain merchants in the Dutch East Indies organized a company with extremely ambitious goals. The company has a close relationship with the Japanese Porcelain Exporters Association and intends to dominate the entire Dutch East Indies porcelain market. The company also invited several Chinese merchants and five European merchants to participate and stipulated the import volume and prices of each merchant, etc. This approach will inevitably have a great impact on the local porcelain industry, so the Dutch East Indies authorities had no choice but to take this emergency measure. If this statement is accurate, then the restriction of Japanese porcelain imports is still the Japanese's own fault. What fault can one find with others? Moreover, the quota issued by the Dutch East Indies government is 100% of last year's import volume, and it has not absolutely prohibited the import of Japanese goods.

Currently, Japanese goods do occupy a large part of the porcelain sold in the Dutch East Indies market, but the porcelain produced in Jiangxi and Shantou in our country is also quite a lot. According to today's telegraphic news, Japanese porcelain merchants are very indignant at the Dutch East Indies' porcelain import restriction law and have already stopped shipping. This is indeed an excellent opportunity for our country's porcelain industry to develop in the Dutch East Indies. Our country's porcelain merchants should not let this opportunity pass by.

Unprecedentedly Severe Drought in Southern Anhui 89

Only Seen Once in Eighty Years

Farmers Swarm Out to Seek Food

Wuhu Communication: The severe drought in various counties in southern Anhui has now reached an irremediable point. The crops have withered, and the beans and grains have turned green. Millions of acres of farmland in Nanling, Wuwei, Tongcheng, and Chaoxian counties can be burned and set ablaze. The elders say that the disaster situation is comparable to the Xianfeng Sixth Year of the Qing Dynasty. It is truly a catastrophe only seen once in eighty years. In towns and villages in various counties, those who have no harvest have already had their entire families seeking food. Those with a little accumulated grain can hardly provide a full meal for many people. Therefore, those who were being fed have been transformed into food seekers in an instant. As the number of food seekers increases day by day, the scope is also becoming wider and wider. In Wuhu, refugees from various counties have been passing through the area every day recently. It is now the autumn harvest season, but there is such a tragic situation. If the harsh winter and barren spring arrive, it will be even more unthinkable. Although the rice price in Wuhu has been suppressed and stabilized by the official and rice industry groups at no more than ten yuan per stone and exports are prohibited, rice merchants hoard and speculate, selling at high prices, still above twelve yuan per stone. A small amount of new grain is sold at around eight yuan. The commissioner's office has recently issued a notice to investigate and prohibit such practices. If anyone deliberately violates the order or acts in defiance, they will be severely punished once discovered. The Commissioner's Office, in view of the tragic situation of the displacement of disaster victims in Wuwei, Nanling, and other counties, and upon receiving the request of representatives of disaster victims from various counties, has distributed emergency relief and has submitted a report to the provincial government, the Relief Association, and the Three-Province Bandit Suppression Headquarters, requesting assistance. (The Eleventh)

Attention Songjiang Residents Regarding the Land Tax Corruption Case 90

Zhang Huanzhi Petitions Chairman for Thorough Investigation and Strict Punishment

Zhu Zhaosheng Requests Attention to Ye Zongcheng's Safety

Songjiang Dispatch: Zhang Huanzhi, a citizen of this county, yesterday petitioned Chairman Chen for a thorough investigation and strict punishment regarding the land tax corruption case. The original petition stated, "Jin Tigan, the Magistrate of Songjiang County, Che Zhao, the Chief of the Finance Section, and Ye Zongcheng, the Director of the Tax Collection Office, have jointly embezzled a substantial amount of land tax. I petition for an investigation and punishment to deter corruption. The conversion of land tax to grain transport in this county began in the 18th year of the Republic [1929]. At that time, Che Zhao was the Director of the Finance Bureau, She Yingduo was the Chief of the Collection Section, and Ye Zongcheng was the Director of the First Land Tax Collection Office (formerly known as the Huating Grain Depot, also known as the East Depot). The registration and issuance of tax bills were handled by these two individuals. The East Depot was responsible for 34,639 mu of land north of the Pu River, with a converted grain transport quota of 3,260 shi and some odd amounts. All landholders have cleared their payments annually. South of the Pu River, there were 84,960 mu of land, with a converted grain transport quota of 7,039 shi and some odd amounts. Not all landholders fully complied with the payment, especially those in coastal villages who resisted due to poor soil quality and inability to pay. This situation was addressed by Shen Bingchen, Xiao Zengrong, and Shen Binde, who served as Bureau Chiefs, but remained unresolved. Last year in April, Magistrate Jin arrived in Songjiang, and the Finance Bureau was merged. Che Zhao was retained as the Chief of the Finance Section because he was familiar with the land tax situation during the tenures of She and the two Shens. In September of that year, Magistrate Jin, taking advantage of the resistance to paying the converted grain transport quota by landholders in coastal villages, colluded with Chief Che and Director Ye, falsely claiming that land north of the Pu River was actually south of it. They reported to the Provincial Finance Department, stating that the grain transport quota south of the Pu River was over 10,000 shi (actually over 7,000 shi) and that no revenue had been collected for four years (actually, over 100,000 yuan had been collected over the years). They requested a 60% reduction from the assessed amount, effectively collecting only 40%, and sought to use the surplus from the 22nd year to offset the 18th year. In October, the Finance Department approved the request with Directive No. 79. They deducted the originally converted grain transport of over 10,000 shi from the actual assessed amount in the autumn censuses of the 18th, 19th, 20th, and 21st years. The actual collected amount for the 22nd year was then listed as 40% of the converted grain transport quota for the 18th year, amounting to over 4,000 shi. They filled out forms and reported this to both the Provincial Finance Department and the Jiangsu Education Expenses Management Office. In May of this year, Magistrate Jin and Chief Che ordered the map compilers and Director Ye to create and issue registers as before, without complying with the Provincial directive to reduce the converted grain transport quota to 40%. These registers were stamped and stored in the East Depot. Magistrate Jin and Chief Che, by feigning a reduction, were not only embezzling over 100,000 yuan of the already collected but not remitted converted grain transport quota from the north of the Pu River since the 18th year, but also attempting to embezzle the 60% tax reduction granted for the 22nd and 23rd years. Their deception of superiors and harm to the country and its people is clearly evident. This inside story was reported by citizen Lu Boxin to the County Party Headquarters in June of this year. Director Ye then resigned on his own initiative. On the first day of last month, Magistrate Jin appointed Yang Yunwen as Ye's successor to ease the tension and find a way to cover up the matter. This was discovered by Zhu Zhaosheng, the Director of the County Education Bureau, who, concerned about the educational funds, petitioned the County Government to investigate. As a result, Magistrate Jin had no choice but to place Ye under supervision, using him as a scapegoat, and ordered Ye to confess in order to reduce his own crime of concealment. At the same time, he petitioned the Provincial Finance Department to correct the portion of the converted grain transport from the north of the Pu River, stating that it was not within the scope of the original reduction plan. At the beginning of this month, he ordered the map compilers in the south of the Pu River to re-create the collection registers for the 23rd year, reducing the converted grain transport quota to 40%. The contradictions and private corruption are glaring. Before the case was discovered, they included the north of the Pu River in the list of surplus collections. After the case was discovered, they excluded the north of the Pu River from the surplus collections. They treated national taxes as a source of profit, the Finance Department as a puppet, official documents as a game, and government orders as worthless rags. The grace of the provincial government in caring for the people and reducing taxes was turned into a tool for these individuals to profit from. Previous Directors of the Finance Bureau never underreported even a single cent of the actual collected and uncollected amounts. After Magistrate Jin deceptively obtained approval from the Finance Department, he deducted over 10,000 shi of converted grain transport from the old arrears of land tax from the 18th to the 21st years, in order to achieve his embezzlement goal. When the inside story was revealed, he shifted the blame to Director Ye to cover his own tracks. I ask, who was the one who deceptively reported the surplus collection? Since the Finance Bureau was merged, the County Government has been the competent authority for the county's finances. Even if Magistrate Jin was not familiar with the situation, Chief Che was an expert in handling the conversion of grain transport. How could he not know how many shi were north of the Pu River and how many mu were south of it? Since over 10,000 shi of converted grain transport from the East Depot was approved for reduction and surplus collection by Directive No. 79, the tax money overcollected by Director Ye and others should be fully refunded. As a Party member and a lawyer, Huanzhi could not bear to see the Provincial directive on tax reduction and surplus collection be used to enrich corrupt officials. Therefore, he published a notice in the newspaper to inform all landholders in the north and south of the Pu River to present their stamped receipts for the converted grain transport from the 18th to the 21st years as soon as possible, so that evidence of Director Ye and others' embezzlement of tax money could be collected and reported truthfully. Since the announcement was made, only six days have passed, but numerous landholders have come to register, nearly wearing out the threshold. However, on the 10th of this month, I received a letter No. 668 from the Songjiang County Government, which stated, 'To whom it may concern, upon reading the notice published in the Songjiang Public News, concerning your announcement to landholders (newspaper attached), it does not conform to the facts. It has been verified that the portion of converted grain transport north of the Pu River is not within the scope of the original plan approved for tax reduction and surplus collection last year. Enclosed is Announcement No. 104 regarding this case for your reference, in order to avoid misunderstandings,' etc. This announcement was issued on August 9th of this year, stating that in June of this year, it was discovered that former Director Ye collected the full amount of the converted grain transport from the south of the Pu River, and also included the north of the Pu River in the surplus collection. The former Director's concealment was truly deserving of punishment, etc. But while Director Ye deserves punishment, do Magistrate Jin and Chief Che deserve no punishment? According to the old arrears of land tax tables and the final accounts for the 22nd year and the budget for the 23rd year, which Magistrate Jin submitted to the Provincial Finance Department and the Provincial Education Expenses Management Office, over 10,000 shi of converted grain transport was deducted from the 18th to the 21st years, and over 4,000 shi of converted grain transport was surplus collected in the 22nd and 23rd years. Therefore, it is beyond doubt that the converted grain transport from both the north and south of the Pu River was within the scope of tax reduction and surplus collection. Land tax collection is of utmost importance, especially since the converted grain transport north of the Pu River totals 3,260 shi. The competent authority should not be allowed to conceal and jointly embezzle it. Therefore, I petition your Excellency to investigate and punish them strictly in order to deter corruption and emphasize taxation. In addition to submitting this separately to the Ministry of Finance and the Jiangsu Provincial Government, I respectfully submit it to Chen, the Chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government." Respectfully submitted by Zhang Huanzhi, a citizen of Songjiang.

Furthermore, Zhu Zhaosheng, the Director of the County Education Bureau, believes that Ye Zongcheng, who is in custody, is old and ill, and that an accident would have serious consequences. He sent a special telegram to the province requesting the County Magistrate to pay close attention. The original telegram is as follows: "To Chen, Chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government in Zhenjiang, and Zhao, Director of the Provincial Finance Department, for your review: Ye Zongcheng, the Director of the First Land Tax Collection Office in Songjiang, has defaulted on taxes and embezzled converted grain transport, amounting to a large sum. The County Party Headquarters and this Bureau have reported the matter, and the County Government has placed him under supervision. However, the Director is old, ill, and deeply addicted to opium. It is said that during his custody, his addiction triggered asthma, and he is on the verge of death. This case is of great importance and will involve many others. If the Director dies in custody, there will be no living witness to the accomplices in the corruption, and the large sum of public funds will be impossible to recover. Therefore, I urgently request that you telegraph the County Magistrate of Songjiang to pay attention to his life's safety, so that he can be treated for his addiction while in custody (according to the new regulations, he should be registered), and prevent evil-doers from plotting his death. This would be fortunate for the overall situation. Zhu Zhaosheng, Director of the Songjiang County Education Bureau, respectfully implores." (12th)

All Salt Merchants in Bengbu Suspend Business 91

Banks Refuse to Terminate Loan Agreements for Transportation Permits

The Government Temporarily Sells Salt for Civilian Consumption

Bengbu Dispatch: The salt market here has always been freely traded, often exhibiting a chaotic appearance. Last autumn, Miao Qiujie, the Salt Commissioner of Lianghuai, changed it to a rotational sales system, with quotas drawn by lot. At that time, banks such as the China Transportation Bank and the Shanghai Bank in Shanghai, seeing the security of the salt business, pre-paid field taxes of up to 900,000 shi to the salt authorities. They loaned transportation permits to salt merchants in Bengbu, collecting substantial profits (there are thirty-six licensed salt merchants operating in Bengbu, who have jointly formed a Huai Salt Sales Office). The banks and the merchants agreed on an interest rate of 1%, and the banks also lent money to river salt merchants in Bengbu, limited to 250,000 shi (because the pre-paid field taxes of 900,000 shi were sufficient to cover the annual sales on both sides of the Huai River in northern Anhui and Henan), in order to avoid affecting the sales of vehicle-transported salt. This agreement has now lasted for a year. River salt sales have reached 650,000 shi. Recently, the Salt Commissioner of Lianghuai planned to restore the free trade system starting from September 1st. The vehicle-transported salt merchants, due to the impact of river salt sales on their stockpiled salt last year, have not yet started sales. The intangible loss per shi, compounded by the new taxes, is more than one yuan higher. Now that the government is restoring the old system, they will inevitably suffer from the encroachment of new salt, and the losses will be even greater. Last month, they jointly sent a letter to the Shanghai banks concerned, requesting the termination of the agreements or a reduction in interest rates in order to maintain their capital. After several exchanges of letters and telegrams, the Shanghai banks ultimately refused. In order to express their determination, the merchants have suspended business since the 6th of this month. Currently, the salt stores in the port have about 20,000 shi of salt, which is only sufficient to meet the needs of the people in twenty-three counties in northern Anhui and eastern Henan for ten days. If this is not resolved for a long time, there will be a shortage of salt. Huang Jingwu, the commissioner of the Bengbu Salt Tax Collection Office, has come forward to mediate. Before a decision is made by both parties, the government will temporarily release some packages of stockpiled salt for sale in order to maintain the food supply for the people. The salt money will be temporarily stored in the Central Bank. The merchants believe that this is acceptable, but the banks have not yet agreed. The situation is very serious. (August 9th, Special Correspondence from this newspaper)

Additional Problems Arise in the Songjiang Land Tax Corruption Case 92

Ye Zongcheng, the Director of the First Land Tax Collection Office in this county, was involved in the land tax conversion corruption case. The County Government is currently supervising the new Director, Yang Yunwen, in conducting a thorough investigation. However, before one wave subsides, another arises. Changes to Patrol Officers in the Public Security Bureau 93

Dispute Over Rickshaw Licenses in Wuxi City and Countryside 94

There are currently over 2,200 rickshaws in this city, crowding the city walls and competing for business, resulting in an oversupply and severely affecting the rickshaw business. After the completion of the Xiyi Provincial Highway, Xin Genji, the owner of a rickshaw company, petitioned for the issuance of additional rickshaw licenses in accordance with regulations in order to operate on that road. However, the authorities, believing that the existing vehicles already constituted an oversupply, did not issue a single license, making it difficult to hire rickshaws in rural areas. Now, Xin Genji argues that among the existing 2,200 rickshaws, over 700 were issued by the Municipal Board of Directors before the ninth year of the Republic [1920], and no security deposit was required at that time, which is inconsistent with the current regulations. Given the current oversupply of vehicles in the city, vehicles without security deposits can be banned uniformly. At the same time, rickshaw licenses for highways such as Xiyi and Xicheng can be issued separately in accordance with the established regulations, so that the supply and demand of rickshaws in the city and countryside can be balanced, maintaining the livelihood of the rickshaw business. Therefore, he specially petitioned the County Construction Bureau for review. However, the matter was learned by the Rickshaw Guild, which, fearing that the vehicles without security deposits would be banned by the authorities, was greatly alarmed. Yesterday, they convened a meeting of the executive committee and decided to convene a general meeting of members on the 13th of this month to discuss countermeasures.

Magistrate Yan Resigns Due to Illness 95

Yan Shenyu, the Magistrate of this county, has been diligent and capable in his work since taking office over a year ago, achieving remarkable results. When the Gu Renfa and Li Shuyun case occurred this spring, he once requested to resign, but it was not approved. The local community was deeply fortunate. However, recently, Mr. Yan suddenly claimed that his body was weak and his energy was insufficient, and that he was unable to handle the heavy workload. A few days ago, he went to the Provincial Department to personally request Yu Minting, the Director, to resign. Director Yu sincerely persuaded him to stay and encouraged him. However, after Yan returned to Wuxi, he formally submitted a petition to the Provincial Department yesterday, requesting approval to resign. Upon hearing the news, various circles in the local community have telegraphed the province one after another, requesting that he be retained.

Reaction to the Price Reduction of the Xicheng Bus 96

Because it had not obtained the approval of the Provincial Department, the Xicheng Long-Distance Bus Company reduced its fares without authorization, resulting in backlash from private car businesses. At 8:00 a.m. on the 11th, drivers drove their private cars to the No. 1 Bridge on the Xicheng Road and blocked the road, preventing Xicheng buses from passing, causing a great uproar. The police station sent police to the scene to maintain order and restore traffic. The drivers then went to the local authorities to petition for relief and fair treatment. Zhang Fulin, the Director of the Construction Bureau, summoned Sun Chenchu, the manager of the Xicheng Company, and Cao Xuemei, Yang Zhaoqing, and Zhang Shaoyan, representatives of the private car business, to the bureau for a discussion. As a result, (1) The Xicheng Company's reduction in fares will not be implemented before it receives approval from the Provincial Department. (2) Private car owners must not engage in any further actions that disrupt traffic. Cao Xuemei and other representatives of the private car owners then made three verbal requests: 1. Requesting a reduction in road maintenance fees. 2. Requesting the restoration of the previous parking locations. 3. Before the fare reduction is implemented, the bus tickets should be stamped, and Sun Yizhuo, the Director of the Vehicle Management Office, will be responsible for inspection to prevent fraud. Director Zhang stated that the first two requests were difficult to fulfill in the current situation, but the third request would be granted. At the same time, the private car owners issued a declaration stating the circumstances of the large buses damaging the private car businesses. Given this conflict, it is unknown how it will be resolved.

Manager of Jiangyin Tiger News Sentenced for Extortion 97

Du Kunao, the manager of the Tiger News, a three-day publication, was accused of attempting to extort Wu Dayuan, the accountant of the factory, by using scandalous reports from Rongxi. After summoning both parties and witnesses for questioning, the County made its final ruling yesterday (11th) at 9:00 a.m. Du Kunao was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment for attempted extortion.

The Declining Lianghuai Salt Industry in Zhenjiang 98

The Lianghuai salt industry is the main business in northern Jiangsu. Its annual production accounts for more than 40% of the country. Almost everyone along the coast relies on this for a living. According to statistics, the number of salt farmers reaches more than one million, and the number of salt workers is even double that. Therefore, no less than three million people in northern Jiangsu rely on Huai salt for their livelihoods. However, in recent years, it has been declining. Although the authorities have been determined to rectify it, the fundamental issues have not been resolved. In particular, the people in the salt areas have weak self-defense capabilities, heavy and miscellaneous taxes, and difficult transportation routes, which are the main reasons for their decline. Therefore, from spring to now this year, it is reported that only 5 million dan of salt have been produced and only 1.2 million dan have been sold. Compared with the 18th year of the Republic (the golden age), it has fallen by more than half. Exploring the reasons, there are only three: (1) There are many bandits in the coastal salt areas, and the salt farmers have weak self-defense capabilities. The salt they boil and dry is often robbed. What is more, the unemployed salt farmers in recent years, every time they see salt being dried in the summer and autumn, form groups of dozens and either rob or destroy it (by drawing seawater into the ponds). These are the so-called salt smugglers. Salt farmers have to guard against bandits from the outside and smugglers from the inside. Their mental suffering is extreme. If they are robbed by bandits and smugglers, their hard work for a year will be in vain, and their livelihood for the whole year will be cut off. Therefore, due to the lack of security for salt farmers, many abandon this industry and seek other ways. (2) Among the salt areas of Lianghuai, in addition to the national tax levied by the central government, various salt affairs agencies and local agencies also levy heavy taxes, such as stove tax, pot tax, and levee maintenance fees. The number of items is too numerous to mention. Although the Lianghuai Salt Transportation Office planned to reduce them last year, it was only empty talk. The livelihood of salt farmers is already difficult to maintain, and they still have to respond to these exorbitant taxes. They cannot afford it, but if they are forced to pay, they will only tend to change their careers. (3) After the salt products are produced in the production area, they must be transported out for sale. There are three routes: one is by vehicle, that is, from Banpu, take the Longhai train and transport it to various lead lands in Anhui and Henan; one is by sea, that is, from Dabao in Haizhou, take a sea ship, go out to the sea, enter Wusongkou, and go upstream along the Yangtze River to Shierwei to unload, then change to sailboats and transport it to various lead lands in the Yangtze River; one is by river, that is, from Xiba Town in Qingjiangpu, use sailboats to go out of Hongze Lake, pass through Changhuai and reach Bengbu, Linhuai Pass and other places, and transport it to Anhui, Henan, Hubei and other provinces. Recently, only the vehicle transportation route is smooth. Sea transportation has caused great disputes. According to the old practice, after being transported into the Yangtze River by sea ships, they must be unloaded at Shierwei in Yangzhou and changed to sailboats. Now, in order to facilitate transportation, the authorities plan to use ships to transport them all the way to Shierwei for unloading. Therefore, tens of thousands of salt workers in Shierwei who rely on sailing for their livelihoods have risen up in opposition and petitioned the central government to fight for their survival. Therefore, in effect, sea transportation has been suspended from spring to now. As for the river transportation route to Hongze Lake, which is a major route, it has long been occupied by bandits, and salt merchants regard it as a dangerous place, so river transportation is only nominal. What is more, in recent years, because Huai salt is difficult to transport and there is a shortage of salt in the various lead lands of the Yangtze River and Huai River, they have purchased refined salt to replace it. Because refined salt companies have the opportunity to take advantage of, they are all competing to produce it to meet the demand, so although Huai salt is sometimes transported to the lead lands by vehicle, the market is full of refined salt to compete with it, and the outcome is already inevitable. To sum up the above, the reduction in Huai salt production this year is worrying, but looking to the future, it is even more worrying. The livelihood of salt farmers has become a problem, and the state's tax revenue is also short, and the impact is both deep and significant. I have described the actual situation to share with readers.

Haimen Cracks Down on Drug Organization 99

The county is filled with drugs, which is the best of the counties in northern Jiangsu.
