Educational News

Recent Reforms in Secondary Education (Part 1) 212

Talks with Persons in Charge of the Ministry of Education

Recently, there has been much social commentary on the secondary education system. A reporter went to the Ministry of Education to inquire about the ministry's views. An important official of the ministry then gave a responsible statement, which is recorded below:

The attitude of society recently is clearly different from that of a few years ago. In the past, everyone only respected education in words. In practice, everyone did not pay attention to education funding, school atmosphere, or the establishment or closure of schools. Recently, people in society have paid very close attention to education. This phenomenon may be a premonition of major educational reforms, which we find deeply gratifying. The Ministry and local education administrative authorities, as well as all those engaged in education, should carefully consider and accept criticisms or suggestions from all parties. However, critics are sometimes not very clear about the content of the current system and other facts. Therefore, the following is a separate explanation of various recent facts related to secondary education, so that those who discuss them can better understand the content of the system and the reform plans that have been carried out, which will make all discussions more beneficial.

(1) Problems with the Secondary Education System 213

Previously, the secondary education system adopted a system of merging middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools. Junior high schools could also set up vocational courses, and senior high schools could combine ordinary normal schools and vocational courses. This system confused the facilities of various types of education and diversified the objectives. As a result, middle school education could not develop, and normal school vocational education was mostly empty. This is an obvious historical vestige. In the past, the reason for advocating the merger of middle schools was that middle schools with vocational and normal school courses would make it easier for students to transfer and adapt, which was suitable for the development of personality, the so-called horizontal and vertical activity system. However, in practice, vocational skills were not fully cultivated, and normal school education did not have professional training, which led to a gradual decline in standards. As a result, the three objectives of making a living, teaching, and going to higher education could not be achieved. In view of the above facts, the Ministry has recently completely separated normal and vocational education from the scope of middle schools, so that ordinary middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools are established separately, with clear objectives and strict training. Ordinary middle schools continue primary school training and serve as a ladder for the study of advanced academics. Normal schools cultivate sound primary school teachers and provide professional training. Vocational schools cultivate the skills of young people to make a living, enabling them to be self-reliant in production. In this way, the complete purpose of ordinary middle schools can be achieved, and the mission undertaken by vocational normal schools can be completed. Therefore, in terms of the current system, the so-called secondary education actually includes three types of separately established schools: middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools.

(2) The Problem of the Distribution of Middle School Education Funds 214

In recent years, the state of secondary education shows that general middle schools are developing exceptionally rapidly, while vocational and normal education are making little progress, especially vocational education. This is a major ailment in recent secondary education, and society is blaming it partly on this. The Ministry of Education's reform of secondary education has also focused on this point recently. According to the 1930 statistical report on secondary education, the number of general middle schools accounts for approximately two-thirds of the total number of secondary schools, the funding accounts for approximately three-quarters, and the number of students exceeds three-quarters. However, the number of vocational schools is less than one-tenth, the funding is only one-tenth, and the number of students is less than seven percent. Even these few vocational schools mostly have crude and simple content and equipment. This kind of distorted development of secondary education not only leads to a lack of qualified teachers in primary schools, but also prevents middle school graduates whose family circumstances or academic abilities limit them from pursuing further education from engaging in occupations because general middle schools (whose main purpose is preparatory training for further education) lack training in production skills. If this continues, not only will the entire secondary education system fail, but also the most serious social problems of the present will inevitably increase day by day. Since the Ministry of Education has adopted the principle of independent establishment for the three types of secondary schools, and in view of the above-mentioned serious situation, it cannot but correct the development trends of secondary education. Therefore, after investigating the actual situation in various provinces and cities last autumn, it formulated standards for the establishment and funding allocation of secondary schools in various provinces and cities, in order to correct the distorted development of the past. The established funding allocation standards stipulate that the funding for vocational schools in each province and city should not be lower than 35% of the total budget for secondary education, the funding for normal schools should not be lower than 25%, and the funding for general middle schools should be limited to 40%. It is also stipulated that each province and city must revise its education budget in accordance with this principle before the beginning of the 1934 fiscal year, establish and formulate a specific plan for phased implementation, and fully achieve the above-mentioned standards before the 1937 fiscal year. It is also stipulated that the new funding after the 1934 fiscal year should be used primarily for vocational and normal education. Those who fail to increase their funding should gradually reduce the corresponding amount of funding for middle schools from the existing funding to expand vocational and normal education. However, the reduction in the number of middle schools must still take into account the balanced development of middle school education throughout the territory and its performance. Currently, the provinces and cities that have followed the Ministry's order to handle and carefully determine the phased reform plan based on the budgetary situation of the province include Hubei, Jiangxi, Guangdong, Anhui, Henan, Fujian, Zhejiang, Sichuan, Yunnan, Suiyuan, Ningxia, Weihaiwei, Chahar, and Beijing. Other provinces and cities, such as Hebei, Hunan, Shaanxi, Shanxi, Jiangsu, Shandong, Gansu, Shanghai, and Qingdao, have also drafted and submitted plans, which are being revised by the Ministry of Education and will be completed soon. If this reform is completed, the distorted state of secondary education in the future can be changed, and the goal of production education can be partially realized. (To be continued)

Chinese Chemical Society

Annual Meeting Closed Yesterday 215

Members Read Papers and Review Chemical Terminology

Today, a Full-Day Tour of Major Factories in the Northern District of Shanghai

The Second Annual Meeting of the Chinese Chemical Society closed yesterday. Papers were read and chemical terminology was reviewed in the morning, a public banquet was held by the Commercial Press at noon, a tour of Wusong was conducted in the afternoon, and an annual banquet was held at the Hua An Hotel in the evening. Details are recorded separately as follows:

Reading of Papers 216

Papers were read in the Engineering Hall at 8:00 a.m. More than 90 members attended, including Shao Jialin, Xu Mingcai, and Chen Yuguang. Zneg Zhaolun chaired. The papers were as follows: (1) Zhang Jiangshu and Liu Yanming's Solubility of Cuprous Chloride in Alcoholic Hydrogen Chloride; (2) Zhang Jiangshu and Cha Yade's Solubility of Cuprous Chloride in Agricultural Hydrochloric Acid; (3) Lu Miannan's New Quantitative Method for Gold; (4) Yang Shuxun's Theory of the Biuret Reaction; (5) Tao Weisun et al.'s Research on Huangyan Oranges and Research on Fuqiao Oil; (6) Yuan Kai, Wan Ce, and Wen Xiangxing's Research on the Effect of Time and Temperature on the Iodine Value of Tung Oil; (7) Han Zukang's Accuracy of the SundStrom's Bicarbonate Determination Method; (8) Li Fangxun et al.'s Conductivity of Gertz Reagent; (9) Li Xun et al.'s Ionization Constant of Benzoic Acid; (10) Yu Junyuan et al.'s New Separation of Copper and Tungsten and Analysis of Animal Bones in North China. It ended at 10:00 a.m.

Terminology Review 217

After the papers were read, a meeting of the Chemical Terminology Review Committee was held. Wu Chenglu, Chen Yuguang, Chen Kezhong, Zeng Zhaolun, Ma Jie, and Li Fangxun attended. Wu Chenglu chaired. It was resolved: (A) Chemical translations are divided into (1) naming principles, (2) instruments and equipment, (3) terminology, (4) elements, (5) chemical engineering; (B) except for the first item, which has been published, the second item is under review, the third item is being compiled, the fourth item is being drafted, and the fifth item is planned to be done in cooperation with the Chinese Chemical Industry Association and the Chemical Engineering Society; (C) except for principles, the rest are arranged in the order of Western letters, and a separate Chinese index is compiled; (D) chemical machinery and equipment are all classified into the second category; (E) personal names are temporarily listed in the original name, and re-translated after the standard for translating personal names and place names is available; (F) the references in the terminology must fully and in detail note the original book; (G) After the terminology is published, it will be revised every three years based on criticisms and opinions from all parties. The meeting was adjourned.

Commercial Public Banquet 218

At noon, the Commercial Press of this city held a public banquet for members at the Bankers' Association, with Wang Yunwu and Zhang Shuliang and others providing attentive hospitality. There Were Enthusiastic Words of Encouragement at the Banquet 221

National Disaster is Not to be Feared, We Must Save the Nation and Restore National Determination

When Going to the West, Pay Attention to Observation, Absorb Culture, and Supplement What Our Country Lacks

| Mayor Wu Chaired, Yan Huiqing, Li Zhaohuan, Pan Gongzhan, Mu Ouchu, and Liu Zhanen Spoke in Succession |

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau and 34 other groups of the Global Chinese Students Federation held a send-off meeting for this year's students studying abroad at the New Asia Restaurant Hall yesterday afternoon. The details are recorded as follows:

The attendees included Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Ambassador to Russia Yan Huiqing, Municipal Education Bureau Director Pan Gongzhan, Jiaotong University President Li Zhaohuan, Shanghai University President Liu Zhanen, Local Association Mu Ouchu, Aviation Association Lin Wojiang, Municipal Education Bureau Ma Chonggan, Yang Zhi of the Global Students Federation, Zhu Shaoping, Zhang You of Fudan University, Liao Maoru of Guanghua University, Huang Zhaoxiong and Xu Zeyu of the Municipal Education Association, Shi She of the China Vocational Education Society, Chen Jicheng and Xu Zexiang of the China School Education Federation, Liu Zhanen of the International Problems Research Association, Ma Chonggan of Shen Bao, Hu Shuyi of Xinwen Bao, Xia Kaiming of Shishi Xinbao, Xu Zexiang of Chen Bao, Zhu Yixin of Min Bao, Xia Menghuan of Zhonghua Daily, Li Dachao of Zhongshan Cultural and Educational Center, Wu Hanfang and Xu Xingchu of the International Society, Lin Jun of the French Literature Society, Chen Kecheng of the Municipal Government, Huang Jingwan of Commercial Press, Xu Jian of Datong, Shen Siqi of the World, Gu Benfan of the Mainland News, and US Consul General Kenningham, Deputy Consul Anya, Commercial Counselor Shi Fanglai, Belgian Consul Fang Fei, Deputy Consul He Naier, and students studying abroad Wu Youlin, Wang Yukai, etc., more than 300 people,

Send-off Situation The meeting started at 4:00 p.m., chaired by Mayor Wu, recorded by the Chinese Shorthand Society, foreign guests received by Zhu Shaoping and Yang Qian, students studying abroad received by Wu Deyi and Ye Xinan, etc. After the formal ceremony, Mayor Wu delivered the opening speech, followed by Yan Huiqing, Li Zhaohuan, Pan Gongzhan, Mu Ouchu, Liu Zhanen, etc., who spoke in succession. Next, Guan Xing, Cai Shaoxu, Jiang Dingxian, Chen Youxin, etc. sang solos, piano and violin solos. Next, student representatives Wu Youlin and Wang Yukai replied. The Global Students Federation presented a guide to staying abroad, and Hua An Society sent the Huamei Monthly. Finally, refreshments were served and a photo was taken before the meeting adjourned.

Mayor's Speech Chairman Mayor Wu Tiecheng delivered the opening speech, saying, "Today is the send-off of this year's students studying abroad by various groups in Shanghai. Shanghai is a transportation hub, so students from all over the country who go abroad every year mostly pass through Shanghai. Therefore, Shanghai has a send-off every year. In recent years, China has been plagued by internal and external troubles, and all the many students going abroad to study is a hopeful thing for China's future, because China has been suffering from internal and external troubles and needs to cultivate a large number of useful people to save the country and solve the current major difficulties. You are going abroad to study, not to seek a degree, but to seek knowledge. Going abroad to seek knowledge means being able to apply what you have learned. Therefore, you have two tasks in studying abroad: the first is to seek knowledge, and the second is to observe. Seeking knowledge is to apply it, and we should catch up with the advanced countries. There are many things in European and American countries that can be imitated, but there must be a distinction, and what is the reason for the rapid progress of European and American countries in economy, politics, and education, and why is the progress so fast, is also what you should know. Therefore, in addition to seeking knowledge, you must also observe. In the past, many students who returned from studying abroad failed, and the reason was that they forgot to observe when they were studying abroad. Today, I, on behalf of various groups, offer some advice to the ambitious youth. I hope that you will use the great spirit of our ancestors' culture to create China, revive the nation, and build a strong Republic of China."

Yan's Speech Yan Huiqing's speech briefly stated, "This time, I came to Shanghai from Qingdao to send my little daughter to study in the United States. I am very honored to attend this grand meeting. After I returned to China from Soviet Russia this time, I saw that many Chinese people were pessimistic and felt that China's future had little hope. But seeing this grand meeting today makes me recall the situation when I left Shanghai for the United States forty years ago. Compared with that, I cannot help but be very optimistic. China's current education is much more advanced than it was forty years ago. Now I will tell you about my own experience. First, when you go abroad, don't be afraid because you are a Chinese student. We should treat ourselves as equal to American students. Our China is a country with thousands of years of culture, and it is not something to be ashamed of. We must be bold in seeking knowledge and doing things when we return to China in the future. Second, in addition to studying when we go abroad, we should also participate in extracurricular activities, whether they are games, sports, literary societies, debates, etc., that are related to the school. We should also go to see foreign museums, theaters, churches, and even the situation in foreign families. Only when we know the political, social, educational, and religious situation of foreign countries and study them can we achieve the purpose of studying abroad. Third, why did many Chinese students fail in the past? Because they were too rigid in their studies abroad and could not expand the knowledge of one country to another country. But no matter what country it is, it has its own system. On the one hand, we should study knowledge, and on the other hand, we should pay attention to bringing the advantages of foreign countries to China, so that it can be sinicized, and the Republic of China can be strong."

Compilation of Speeches (1) Li Zhaohuan's speech was divided into three points: (1) Today we are sending you off because you are the representatives of the youth. I hope that after you go abroad, you must work hard to study and make a name for yourselves to win glory for the country. The backwardness of Chinese culture today goes without saying, but building a new culture requires new materials and new methods, which we especially hope you will work hard on. Finally, I hope you will have three attitudes when you go abroad to study: self-respect, self-effacement, and self-esteem. (3) Mu Ouchu's speech was divided into (1) having the power of observation, (2) not being pessimistic, but being optimistic, and (3) paying attention to physical training. (4) Liu Zhanen's speech stated that today I will only give you one word, which is "do." I hope that you will practice the word "do" abroad, and also practice the word "do" after you return to China, not to get promoted and make a fortune, but to seek the welfare of the people.

Economic Special

The Future of Silk Industry Control 223

— Xu Hanchen

The fundamental forms of the silk industry crisis are: firstly, the price of cocoons is as cheap as mud, exceeding the limit that farmers can tolerate for unpaid labor; secondly, the weakness of economic capacity determines that farmers can only desperately abandon the cultivation of improved varieties and replace them with local varieties; and thirdly, farmers abandon or reduce silkworm rearing, resulting in the rapid destruction of mulberry fields and the conversion to other crops. This trend has been more vigorously promoted in the process of ending this year's spring cocoon market. The fundamental decline of the silk reeling industry and the accelerated development of agricultural panic in various forms: In the face of these interactive fundamental threats, the main sideline of the rural areas in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, the silk industry, its future is truly precarious!

The government has long paid great attention to reversing this decline. For example, the National Economic Commission has specially established the Silk Industry Control Committee to undertake this mission. Other examples include Zhejiang, which has been silently implementing its control policy for more than a year under the management of institutions such as the Committee for Managing Improved Sericulture. Since this spring, Jiangsu, under the leadership of the Department of Construction, has also organized the Sericulture Improvement Committee to vigorously promote the control of the entire province's silk industry. With the joint agreement of the Ministries of Finance and Industry and the two provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang to formulate a plan to save the silk industry, more specific provisions have been made for its implementation. In addition to relatively minor measures such as encouraging mulberry planting, improving mulberry gardens, and improving technology, its main direction is to proceed under the two major goals of cocoon market control and silkworm seed control. The control policy has become the government's fundamental plan to resolve the current silk industry crisis, which is already an unquestionable event.

In the plan submitted to the Executive Yuan by the Ministries of Finance and Industry, there is a proposal to improve the method of cocoon collection, aiming to liberate farmers from the exploitation of usury and the middle layer of commercial capitalists, and to "take direct trade between farmers and silk factories as the principle." However, in reality, the control of cocoon markets is clearly not based on this "principle." Its motivation is more or less related to the current financial crisis. Therefore, the control law stipulated by the Jiangsu Department of Construction naturally shifts its focus to articles such as "compelling cocoon collectors to pay a deposit of three yuan per load" (Article 6) and "collecting an improvement fee of twelve yuan for each load of dried cocoons collected" (Article 8)! The relationship between this type of control law, which is purely for increasing tax revenue, and the salvation of the silk industry crisis is truly elusive!

On the other hand, the Fifth Congress of the Jiangsu Provincial Sericulture Improvement Committee passed thirteen "severe crackdown" measures in order to suppress the cocoon market's resistance to control. Among them, Article 4 states, "If any cocoon collector's daily cocoon collection report is found to have underreported the amount, the underreported portion of the cocoons will be confiscated and forfeited to the public." Article 5 states, "If any cocoon collector's cocoons have not been reported for a dried cocoon transport request form and a dried cocoon fee payment certificate and a dried cocoon pass have not been issued, and they transport the cocoons without authorization, the portion transported without a certificate will be confiscated and forfeited to the public." These measures are clearly designed to prevent merchants from evading payment, thus also implying that the specific content of the so-called cocoon market control is actually to collect a disguised tax. Article 9 of the measures also stipulates, "Anyone who impersonates cocoons from model improvement areas as cocoons from ordinary areas in an attempt to avoid paying the sericulture improvement fee will have all of their cocoons confiscated and forfeited to the public." Thus, the only difference between cocoons produced in the so-called model improvement areas and those in ordinary areas is that they have paid an additional fee. Therefore, in the current trend of the government actively promoting sericulture rescue measures by dividing areas, there is the bizarre phenomenon of silk cocoon merchants in Jiangyin County sending a telegram to the Ministry of Industry and the Rural Reconstruction Commission opposing the county's designation as an improvement area and demanding confirmation as an ordinary area. The shadows under the current cocoon market control policy are truly alarming!

In fact, there is not much difference in opinion between the government and the cocoon merchants. Merchants do not need to say anything else except that the policy increases the tax rate, and they do not need to oppose control. Therefore, when the Jiangsu cocoon market's resistance to the control measures caused a great uproar this spring, it was quickly resolved because the government accepted three measures, including "paying an improvement fee of three yuan per load of dried cocoons." However, apart from the huge new tax revenue, it is an issue that we should not ignore whether cocoon market control has reduced the various monopolies and manipulations suffered by farmers from commercial capitalists, or whether it has enabled silk reeling factories to reduce their "cocoon costs" without "cocoon merchants circulating and selling in between."

In this year's spring cocoon market, farmers were still or even more severely exploited by cocoon merchants' monopoly of cocoon prices. The cocoon market guilds in Wuxi, Jiangyin, Shaoxing, Xiaoshan, Haining, and other places determined the maximum price of cocoons long before the opening of the market, and they all had more or less influence on the cocoon market. In Jintan County, in order to implement cocoon market control, the twenty-seven cocoon markets were merged into four, all of which were monopolized by large merchants, who were able to arbitrarily lower prices. As a result, the masses of farmers rose up in resistance, triggering bloody riots. The same facts also reappeared in Xiaoshan (see Daily News in June). The exploitation function of commercial capitalists has not been affected in any way by the vigorous implementation of cocoon market control. In the process of merchants passing on the improvement fees they pay to farmers, they will naturally need to further promote the function of monopoly and price cutting. In this way, cocoon market control has become a policy far removed from the masses of farmers. In addition to painfully selling their cocoons at prices lower than the market price, farmers have no choice but to dry their cocoons and reel silk at home, hoping without any guarantee that the silk market will rebound to save them!

We can easily deduce how much capacity the government's cocoon market control policy, which is implemented in the cocoon sales market, has to save the silk industry panic from its fundamental direction and actual situation.

Of course, in the government's entire system of saving the sericulture industry, its main goal is placed in the silkworm cocoon production process in order to achieve fundamental liberation. Improving silkworm breeds is considered the first step, and silkworm seed control is the concrete means of implementation. But what are the results?

The extreme poverty of the entire rural area and the plummeting price of cocoons make it impossible for farmers to dream of improving the silkworm rearing process. Poverty prompts them to yearn for a good cocoon harvest, while at the same time fundamentally destroying their hope. Farmers in Jiangsu and Zhejiang are generally rapidly returning to rearing local varieties because they have no cash to buy expensive improved silkworm seeds. This situation can be seen in the overproduction of improved varieties this spring. Not only were there two or three hundred thousand more silkworm seeds than needed in Jiangsu Province, but there were also eighty thousand more in Zhejiang Province, which implemented control, and they could not be sold. Silkworm seed control can to some extent force people to rear improved varieties, but it cannot overcome the poverty of farmers, which is the core of the problem!

At present, Jiangsu Province is actively carrying out silkworm seed control and has promulgated eight control measures, which will be implemented in model improvement areas starting in the autumn of the 23rd year of the Republic. The main measures are: (1) Each silkworm household must submit a form reporting the number of silkworm seeds required by June 30 for autumn seeds and October 31 for spring seeds; (2) The seed payment for autumn seeds must be remitted before July 20 of the same year, and the seed payment for spring seeds must be remitted before December 31 of the previous year; (3) After the seed payment in the preceding paragraph is received, silkworm seeds will be allocated according to the seed price paid, but the quantity of seeds received by each silkworm household shall not exceed the quantity reported in advance, and no seeds may be claimed after the deadline. Another most important thing is the unified seed price, which is uniformly five cents per sheet. According to the seed price in Wuxi this spring, the best ones, such as the Tiger brand seeds produced by Dayou Seed Farm, have fallen in price to seven cents, and the Shou Xing and other brands are only selling for four cents per sheet. So how much seed price preference can farmers now get from silkworm seed control? In the above three seed selling methods, the government is indeed very convenient in carrying out its work. It does not have to bear the risk of seed price arrears, nor does it have the drawbacks of inconsistency between silkworm seed production and sales. But there will never be two opposing parties benefiting at the same time. In order for the government to conveniently carry out its so-called control, the burden on farmers has turned into an unexpected increase in responsibility. Under the threat of extreme fluctuations in the market price of silk, the amount of autumn silkworm rearing must be decided by farmers before June 30; even the amount of silkworms that will begin to be raised in March of the following year must now be decided before October of the previous year. Regardless of whether farmers have the ability to make such a decision, the third method forces them to blindly decide; otherwise, they will no longer have any silkworm seeds to receive. Farmers need to bear all the losses of rearing more or less during this long period. In particular, the second method, regarding the pre-deadline payment of seed funds, simply makes it impossible for farmers to accept the good intentions of silkworm seed control. Farmers must pay the seed funds several months before receiving the silkworm seeds. In this way, farmers who are trapped in extreme poverty in the entire agricultural panic are either more oppressed and fall deeper into the clutches of usurers, or they are forced to give up the opportunity to continue silkworm rearing. The facts will tell us after the autumn silkworm rearing begins.

For general ordinary areas, the Jiangsu Province sells silkworm seeds publicly, and the price is one cent higher per sheet (i.e., six cents) (see Article 4, Item B, Paragraph 2 of the control regulations). In addition, there are so-called special circumstances in improved areas, where the selling price is increased by two cents per sheet, i.e., seven cents (same as above, Item C). This difference in public sale prices between model areas and ordinary areas is clearly due to the fact that the government has collected huge improvement fees in the model areas. The blood relationship between the collection of improvement fees and the public sale of silkworm seeds is thus!

Farmers are scattered, and they only silently answer with facts. But the burden that silkworm seed control imposes on merchants, they are not willing to accept silently. In June, the Jiangsu Provincial Government's method of purchasing autumn seeds was: "Selling in Jiangsu Province, each sheet is 7.5 cents, pay 5 cents first, for a total of 320,000 yuan, and the remaining 2.5 cents will be supplemented from the cocoon price after the cocoons are produced. 160,000 yuan can be allocated from the spring cocoon donation for this 320,000 yuan, and the rest will be allocated by the Department of Finance (see Da Wan Bao, June 24); however, recently, "The Jiangsu Provincial Sericulture Improvement Association, in order to take into account the facts, has changed the method again to pay 1.5 cents per sheet first" (see Zhonghua Daily, August 7), which caused the Wuxi, Suzhou, and Wujin Silkworm Seed Industry Association to hold several meetings to oppose it, believing that "the provincial regulations are clearly contrary to the original decrees" and resolutely demanding "the abolition of the order to sell outside the province, and demanding that 5.5 cents per sheet be paid in advance for seed funds, otherwise they will refuse acid immersion." As a result of the petition, the responsible authorities replied: "Regarding the seed price, the Department has stipulated that 5 cents will be given first, excluding 1.5 cents, which has already been paid to each farm, and the remaining 2.5 cents will be re-issued depending on the results of the autumn cocoons" (both seen in the above report). At present, representatives from the three counties are still continuing to petition the province. But in this way, the government no longer needs to "allocate 180,000 yuan from the spring cocoon donation," and it is no longer necessary for the Department to pay 140,000 yuan. However, in order to obtain autumn seeds, farmers had to pay the seed funds to the "Sericulture Improvement Management Committee" at a price of 5 cents per sheet as early as July 20!

The silk industry must be rescued. In addition to measures such as increasing mulberry planting or improving technology, which are still on the planning books, cocoon market control and silkworm seed control have been vigorously promoted, but their future is as described above. Therefore, the solution to the silk industry crisis is still a problem for the Chinese farmers themselves! August 11.

The Way Out of the Silk Industry's Impasse 224

— Xia Daoxiang

丨A Study of the Listing of Chinese Silk on the New York Commodity Exchange丨

In recent years, the export of Chinese silk has been hindered, and the market price of cocoons and silk has repeatedly fallen below the production cost. Farmers planting mulberry trees and raising silkworms have no profit, so they have dug up mulberry trees to plant other crops, resulting in a continuous decrease in cocoon production. Other seed production farms and silk factories have also declared closure and bankruptcy one after another due to operating losses, the number of which is countless. Tens of thousands of workers in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Guangdong, and other places have lost their jobs. The entire silk industry is showing a declining phenomenon. Although the central and local governments have tried to save it, due to the trend of the world economic situation and the weak ability of domestic operators, it is difficult to make any recovery for a while. Just when the people in the national silk industry were sighing in unison, suddenly in May, the news came that the New York Commodity Exchange in the United States, which sells the most silk in the world, planned to list Chinese silk and Italian silk, and allow Chinese and Italian silk to be used instead of Japanese silk for delivery. This is actually a prelude to promoting the sale of Chinese silk to the United States.

Let's explore the motives of this matter and the process of its advancement. Although it is related to the United States itself, how can it be achieved without the promotion of other parties? After all, whether we have the power to promote it or not, we must study the recent situation of Chinese silk's international trade.

The export trade of Chinese silk has always been controlled by foreign merchants. In Shanghai, although several Chinese merchants, such as Hulin, Weicheng, Jingxing, and Tongyun, came out to operate in the past, they all declared closure one after another due to losses. Only Tongyun remains. Recently, Wuxi Yongtai Silk Factory has also sent personnel to the United States to negotiate silk sales, but it is only for the sake of its own silk production. With such weak exporters, how can they have the power to promote and publicize? In addition, the quality of Chinese silk exported to the United States is mixed, and the quantity is decreasing year by year. Now, according to the numbers recorded by the American Silk Association and our Chinese Customs, a table is listed below for reference:

Table of Chinese Silk Exports to the United States in the Last Eight Years (Survey by the American Silk Association, Unit: picul)

Year | Amount of Chinese Silk Exported to the United States | Total Amount of Raw Silk Imported by the United States from Various Countries | Percentage of Chinese Silk in the Total Raw Silk Imports of the United States

(Note) The numbers reported by the Customs are slightly different from those surveyed by the American Silk Association, presumably because a considerable number of Chinese silk exports are indirectly shipped to the United States.

From the above table, it can be seen that Chinese silk exports to the United States amount to only tens of thousands of bales per year, and the types include white and yellow filature silk, white and yellow reeled silk, and gray silk. Moreover, since 1932, the exports have decreased from 60,000-70,000 bales to more than 20,000 bales. Although the reason is said to be the impact of economic recession and rayon, how can we know that it is not caused by the poor quality of Chinese silk! With such a small quantity and mixed quality of Chinese silk, how can it arouse the sympathy of the American silk industry and be promoted?

So, where is the driving force behind this matter? In my opinion, it is in Italy. Why do I say that? Since Prime Minister Mussolini came to power in that country, he has vigorously promoted the revitalization of rural areas, improved trade, and encouraged the silk industry. The output of raw silk has increased year by year, from more than 4 million pounds to more than 10 million pounds. Recently, an emergency relief policy has been implemented, giving silk producers a reward of three lire per kilogram of fresh cocoons. Moreover, for the export of raw silk, international management is sought, and European countries are united to prevent the import of East Asian raw silk (Japanese silk), in order to increase the consumption of Italian and French silk. At the same time, for the export of Italian silk to the United States, various publicity and on-site improvements have been carried out, and the exports have increased sharply from 2,700 bales to more than 19,000 bales, an increase of more than seven times. The recent amount of Italian silk exported to the United States is recorded below:

Table of Italian Silk Exports to the United States in Recent Years (Unit: bale)

Year | Amount of Italian Raw Silk Imported | Total Amount of Raw Silk Imported by the United States | Percentage of Italian Silk in the Total Imports of the United States

From the above, it can be seen that the output of Italy and the amount of its exports to the United States have made considerable progress compared with Italy itself, but from the perspective of the American raw silk market, Italian silk only occupies a very small position of less than 3%. How can it attract the attention of the American silk industry and be promoted? In my opinion, the greatest driving force behind this matter lies in Italy's international publicity. At the same time, Italian merchants such as Ganli, who control the full power of world and American raw silk trade, have played a major role in promoting it, resulting in this result. Chinese merchants are only benefiting from it.

Although the New York Commodity Exchange in the United States has been promoted by Italy's international publicity and Italian merchants such as Ganli, it has also always felt that Japanese silk monopolizes the American market and manipulates market prices. Therefore, it has advocated Chinese and Italian raw silk in order to contain and break the monopoly and seek market stability. The following is a list of the amount of raw silk consumed by the United States from various countries, as surveyed by the American Silk Association, for reference:

Table of Raw Silk Consumption in the United States from Various Countries (Unit: picul), Survey by the American Silk Association

From the above table, it can be seen that the United States consumes about 500,000 piculs of raw silk every year. Among them, more than 85% is Japanese silk, European silk accounts for only less than 3%, and Chinese silk accounts for less than 12%. It is self-evident that the American raw silk market is monopolized by Japan and the market price is manipulated by it. Therefore, the United States often promotes Chinese and Italian raw silk in order to subdue Japanese silk and seek market stability, so as to avoid being oppressed by Japan; at the same time, American importers who operate Chinese and Italian raw silk also help from the side in order to obtain considerable benefits. When the Japanese silk industry authorities received the news that the raw silk department of the New York Commodity Exchange in the United States planned to list Chinese and Italian silk and allow it to be used as a substitute for Japanese silk delivery, they believed that it would have a great impact on Japanese silk exports to the United States. Therefore, the Central Silk Association Council held a meeting in June to discuss this matter. The result was: it was considered that the sale of Japanese raw silk with Italian silk and Chinese silk as substitutes for delivery would make the transaction complicated and there was a risk of lack of proper delivery. This was telegraphed to the New York Commodity Exchange, requesting it to consider carefully. At the same time, Japanese raw silk exporters also publicized to the United States that Chinese and Italian raw silk only supply the United States with 40,000-50,000 bales per year, and their quality is mixed. If they are listed, it will only lead to speculative results of buying and selling short, and the price of silk will fluctuate meaninglessly. Not only will the Japanese silk industry be affected, but also American consumers will feel disadvantaged. Therefore, the New York Commodity Exchange will decide on the case of Chinese and Italian silk being used as substitutes for delivery after discussing it at the raw silk member discussion meeting held on September 6 this year.

Even if the New York Commodity Exchange allows Chinese silk to be listed and allowed to be used as a substitute for delivery, whether our Chinese silk can immediately increase its exports to the United States is still uncertain. However, when Italy is promoting and facilitating the preparations for the United States, Japan is obstructing with various arguments. Although this is inevitable in international commercial competition, we must do our best to deal with the aftermath. Now, based on what I have seen, I will write briefly on the left for the exploration of those who care about the silk industry:

First, cooperate with Italy to promote. Feeling the promotion of the Italians in the past, the Chinese people should work together to cooperate in order to realize the listing and delivery of Chinese and Italian silk in the United States; second, publicize to the United States. Before the raw silk department member discussion meeting of the New York Commodity Exchange on September 6, people in our country's silk industry should make various written and on-site publicity in the United States regarding the listing and delivery of Chinese silk as a substitute, so as to avoid being slandered; third, manage Chinese silk exports to the United States and organize sound institutions. In the past, Chinese silk exports to the United States not only lacked management and control, but also the Chinese merchants who directly operated exports were only the individual sales of Shanghai Tongyun and Wuxi Yongtai Silk Factory. The rest was mostly handled by foreign merchants, resulting in various malpractices. This time, the Japanese side has criticized the mixed quality of Chinese silk and that it cannot be used as a substitute for delivery, and that the number is very small. If it is listed, it will only lead to speculation of buying and selling short, resulting in high and low silk prices. We should ask people in the silk industry to carefully consider, study, and implement ways to improve it. The fundamental methods, I have repeatedly written articles to describe, such as improving the unified quality of Chinese silk, reducing the cost of Chinese silk, and stabilizing the market price of Chinese silk. However, the current situation of the silk industry is still difficult to achieve this. The only way is to implement management and control over Chinese silk exports to the United States, and organize a sound institution for exports to the United States through cooperation between officials and merchants. The methods and principles are tentatively proposed as follows:

A. Before Chinese silk is exported to the United States, whether it is handled by Chinese or foreign merchants, it must be strictly inspected by the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau according to the standards required by American sock factories and silk factories, and only those that pass the inspection are allowed to be exported:

B. It is best that all raw silk prepared for export to the United States be handled by the institution in order to ensure that the quality of the silk sold meets the needs of the United States. At the same time, we must strive to stabilize the market price of Chinese silk in the American market, and do not show high and low prices from time to time, which will cause a bad impression on the Americans;

C. The quality of the silk handled by the institution, whether it is sold on consignment or purchased and resold, must be above standard D, and can be used as a substitute for Japanese silk delivery, and the purchase price cannot be too high in order to compete with Japanese silk sales.

The above views, I dare not say are appropriate, but with opportunities ahead, please silk industry operators rise up and catch up, and make a common effort.

Bond Market Shows Slight Consolidation Last Week 226

Only 96 Bonds Up 30 Cents

The past week, August 6th to 11th, at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange, the market was extremely stable, remaining in a consolidating state, a rare occurrence in the past two months. Previous market prices had been creeping upwards, with the highest prices approaching 80 percent. General expectations had been met, and under normal circumstances, further increases were unlikely. Consequently, large bullish traders were largely exiting their positions, with selling from northern syndicates being particularly strong. The heavy selling on the 4th of the previous week led to further selling from northern syndicates last week. Therefore, even though the 4th no longer sold, the market situation did not improve. This was due to the supply and demand of funds, but the bond market environment should not be underestimated. Huang Fu's return to politics and expected trip north suggest considerable progress on the North China issue. The inflexibility of the Bank Savings Law means that the bonds deposited with the Central Bank in the future will exceed 200 million yuan and cannot be moved. They cannot be sold at highs and bought at lows as freely as before. Other factors, such as banknote reserves, are not included in this figure. Once implemented, the market will inevitably face a shortage of funds. Therefore, if the future situation does not change much, the bond market still has potential for development. The past week was entirely a consolidation, with fluctuating prices in each of the two daily sessions. Slight increases were met with selling pressure, and slight declines were met with buying support. Although there was upward momentum, it was repeatedly suppressed, leading to a decline in market sentiment. The daily fluctuations were only two or three dimes. The most aggressive sellers were from northern syndicates, with significant selling of 76 bonds. The week's market performance resulted in declines of one or two dimes to seven or eight dimes for most bonds, with only 96 bonds up 30 cents. The total transaction volume was 49,751,000 yuan. New York Industrial Stocks See Gains 227

Silver Plan Has Slightly Expansionary Nature

Xinfeng Yanghang reported yesterday (11th) that there were two main events in the New York market: one was the raid on the US dollar by short sellers, and the other was the sharp fall in US government bonds. The reason for both was the public's feeling of danger of inflation. Calculated at 35 yuan per ounce of gold, the US-French exchange rate, the US dollar fell by 1%, so it has exceeded the import point. It is now profitable for foreigners to ship gold into the US. Although the US government claims to allow gold to be imported, no one has tried this experiment yet. Except for gold and silver stocks, the stock market saw gains and losses, with very small differences. Railway stocks were relatively weak. Yang City's steel production fell by 17% to 22%, but steel stocks were still stable. The small exchange market was uneven. Foreigners still believe that silver nationalization is the real precursor to inflation. A Treasury official also admitted that the silver plan "has a slightly expansionary nature," so this business has been somewhat confirmed. US government bonds initially fell by more than two yuan, but rebounded before the close, probably as a result of government maintenance. Domestic bonds also fell, while foreign bonds were flat. Grain prices initially fell sharply by five points (the maximum limit) due to rainfall in drought areas and the government's harvest report not being as bad as generally imagined. Later, it was rumored that rainfall might be insufficient, and buyers became brave, pushing prices back up. In the last minute, many profit-takers emerged, and it was rumored that heavy rain was pouring down everywhere and the temperature was dropping sharply. In addition, limit orders that had not been sold were automatically liquidated, and the market fell again by five points. It is rumored that the crop loss is not as large as generally estimated. At the same time, Agriculture Secretary Wallace announced that crop restrictions for next year would be revised, and public panic reached its peak. The exchange suddenly became a madhouse. Until the final gong closed, there were still large-scale sell orders that could not be executed. The New York Stock Exchange announced after the close of trading today that the short positions at the end of July were slightly higher than at the same time last year. Half-day trading volume was 310,000 shares. The Dow Jones index is listed below:

Spring and Autumn

Records of the Fragrant Imperial Carriage 230

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Unfortunately, no matter how qualified a driver in the world is, it's probably impossible for him to drive without any jolting! At least, the driver who's driving this imperial train for us here doesn't have that skill!

The order to start the train was given, and the train officially began to move. At this time, we were all standing upright in that small court. The Empress Dowager was sitting high on her throne, her face full of smiles, ready to fully enjoy her first train ride. Unexpectedly, the entire train suddenly lurched backward, then suddenly lurched forward, shaking us so hard that we almost fell over. At the same time, many of the Empress Dowager's favorite antiques and jade ornaments, which were placed on small wooden shelves on the wall, fell down because they couldn't withstand the jolt. This really scared me out of my wits! A coolie-like driver dared to shake the Empress Dowager's beloved possessions to the ground. Wouldn't he be severely punished? I think the Empress Dowager probably had such thoughts in her mind at that time. Regardless of whether she actually had those thoughts, we couldn't worry about the driver anymore. We had to take care of ourselves! Because the arrangement of this train was almost entirely handled by me and Qing Shan. The idea of installing these small wooden shelves on the east wall to hold the Empress Dowager's antiques and jade ornaments was also decided by us. Now, before we've even left Beijing, these things have all fallen down with the train's first movement. Who can say there won't be more tricks later as the train moves forward? I think someone among these people will definitely have to sacrifice his head! Of course, I myself can't be sure that the person who gets the knife won't be me. Maybe it will be me! Who can guarantee it? Especially since I had boasted to the Empress Dowager about how thoughtful the arrangements on the train were and how well everything was arranged before I escorted her out of the palace and into the sedan chair. Who knew that less than two hours later, I would get such a contradictory rebuttal. Readers, think about it: What good impression could the Empress Dowager still have of me? (103)

Newcomer's Individual Biography 231

— Qing Qu

The day before yesterday, when I arrived in Shanghai, I saw something at a friend's house that could evoke feelings and express the sigh of the changing times. Thirty years ago, when this friend was still a child, he was a young master, living in luxury. He sat in his study and read for no more than one or two hours, considering his studies complete. He then went with his father in a carriage to eat elaborate meals. Later, he suffered a major misfortune, but even at a young age, he was able to inherit the family business and carefully preserve all the assets, so people called him a young and mature, filial son. But now? Not to mention that his family fortune has declined, his situation is far from what it used to be. However, while I was at this friend's house, before we had met, he called out from upstairs, "Newcomer, you! Pour a cup of tea and ask the guest to sit down." Who would have thought that the person who brought the tea was an old woman with white hair and a tottering gait? Moreover, she recognized me and was able to call me Mr. ×, which surprised me a little. At first, I thought that Shanghai families always called their maids "Nanny," or "Zhang's," "Wang's." Even if they called someone "Newcomer," it wouldn't be someone so old who had lived there for decades. "Oh!" she said to me secretly, "Mr. ×, you know, Young Master × lost tens of thousands in the stock exchange that spring, and then lost tens of thousands in the gold business that winter. Finally, he also got into a lawsuit over real estate disputes. Mr. ×, the old master never would have imagined this back then!" After saying that, tears rolled down her eyes like beads. After hearing these words, I couldn't help but feel a sudden pang of sadness in my heart. I asked her, "How old are you this year?" She said, "I'm already seventy-three years old. I came here when I was only in my thirties, when Young Master × was still in his mother's belly. Now Young Master ×'s son is already twenty years old, married, and has children." I asked her, "You're not really a newcomer; you're an old-comer." She pursed her lips, smiled, and went inside.

After resting for a while, my friend came down from upstairs. Because I had heard the old woman's words, when I met him, my feelings were different from before. I found it difficult to find the right words to say, given the current environment and the conversation. In the end, I exchanged some polite greetings and said, "I just came by on the way today. I'll come to your residence another day for a more detailed chat." After leaving, I thought that the old woman's words were like a white-haired palace maid talking about ancient history. This is her biography.

Trivial Talks on Surveying 232

— Yang Yusheng

How many square miles does China's territory actually cover? If this question is resolved based on the ancient records passed down from our ancestors, it's just a rough estimate, like the Chinese population always being "four hundred million," and it lacks accuracy. People in our country are always worried about the shrinking of our territory, but how much territory do we actually have? Even geography experts probably can't give a precise answer. It's really shameful to say!

As a rule, China's surveying engineering is only used for road construction and river dredging. Surveying the national borders is too troublesome and impractical! Therefore, if other countries don't encroach on China's land, we won't even think about surveying the national borders! Therefore, this article's "trivial talks" are limited to surveying road lines.

The initial step in building a road is surveying. After the road line is determined, the work of purchasing land from the people begins, and only then can construction start. There are many jokes that play out during this process.

When villagers see a group of people carrying "telescopes" and "tape measures" "looking around" and "measuring back and forth" on their fields, they subconsciously know what's going on. Regardless of whether this group of people is practicing surveying or actually planning to build a road, they always shout in a panic-stricken tone, "They're coming to build a road!" It's like everyone is scaring each other about a ghost!

The things used to mark the road line are wooden stakes driven into the ground. For the sake of preventing their fields from being "encircled and bought," the strong ones destroy these wooden stakes at night, while the kind ones secretly move the stakes to another place, with a meaning of "pushing the dead corpse across the border." Therefore, there are many limitations on the surveying project.

We often see news in the newspapers about villagers beating surveyors and burning surveying instruments, but before "beating" and "burning," they also unleash many fierce dogs to scare away the surveyors. It's really stubborn and ridiculous!

This only refers to the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, where the folk customs are relatively good. In the areas of Anhui and Shaanxi, where there are many bandits, it is said that when the Longhai Railway began surveying, there were several times more armed guards with live ammunition than surveying personnel. In China, trying to do some "development" work faces unexpected difficulties. The closed-mindedness of the people is truly regrettable!

Our Country Urgently Needs to Prepare for Scientific Warfare 233

Women in Hedonistic Professions 234

— Zhang Yuqing

Women in Hedonistic Professions.

Does it raise the professional status of women? Even movie stars who crave being on camera are jumping out of the film industry to become dancers. Is this due to the economic downturn or personal decadence? Perhaps it's an unanswerable mystery?

Being a dancer is so much fun! It's both enjoyable and profitable, everyone says. Not necessarily! Nothing is ever that simple, is it? But no one sympathizes with their hardships!

Indeed, successful dancers are flourishing and making money everywhere, but their painful underside far outweighs the dance tickets in their purses!

Even when they want to cry, they have to force a smile and act coquettish to please the guests. The thin silk cheongsam is as drenched as if they just came out of a swimming pool. They keep applying cosmetics containing lead, layer after layer. It's late at night! Their legs are weak and powerless! To satisfy the guests, they can only smoke and drink, using nicotine and alcohol to combat the failing spirit. But the guests? They keep going like a clockwork toy, without stopping, maybe even more energetic than before. After all, they came to enjoy themselves! Of course! There are still more painful cries hidden!

Shanghai Embroidery 235

— Shanghai News Agency

Nowadays, the embroidery businesses in the Jiangsu and Zhejiang areas all write "Gu Embroidery" on their signboards.

Yes, the exquisite quality of Gu Embroidery is worthy of being the best in the country. At the Nanyang Industrial Exposition in the Qing Dynasty, a portrait of the Italian Empress Dowager, hand-made by Ms. Yu Shenshou of Suzhou, was worth 3,000 pounds. Even now, it is still told as a beautiful story.

But, embroidery is fine, but why insist on calling it Gu Embroidery?

It turns out that there's a story worth mentioning.

During the Ming Dynasty, there was a wealthy gentleman in Shanghai named Gu Huihai, who built a Luxiang Garden on nine acres of land northwest of the county seat. His concubines and maids were particularly skilled in embroidery. Landscapes, figures, plumage, flowers, and plants were all lifelike. The works were very valuable.

There was a "Picture of Eight骏," which, it is said, was praised by viewers as "even Zi Ang's brush couldn't match." There was also a "Picture of Venerable One" (i.e., a Buddhist image), for which someone wrote a poem of praise, saying: "The maiden embroiders Buddha, delighting humans and gods, moving the needle like a brush, the silk like paper. The woman of Huating Gu is praised for her divine skill, twirling silk and splitting thread with slender fingers," and so on.

There is a small story behind the "Stopped Needle Picture."

It is said that one day, many distinguished guests gathered in Luxiang Garden. During the conversation, Gu Embroidery was mentioned, and they all praised it highly. Only an old Confucian scholar named Jin disagreed, saying:

"Although embroidery is good, it is unnecessary. In the past, Qian Wentong liked to wear new clothes and wore official attire made of bright red cloud-patterned cloth to court. As a result, the court learned that Songjiang produced cloth, and ordered that it be sent to Beijing as tribute every year, which has harmed the local area to this day. Why doesn't your family engage in weaving, so that visitors to your door only hear the clatter of looms? Wouldn't that be more meaningful than your family's women embroidering day and night, with that expression of stopped needle and silence?"

At that time, Gu Huihai listened and smiled askew at others, saying:

"Don't say this gentleman is an old scholar! Although his wording is straightforward, it is quite charming!"

The next day, he ordered someone to embroider the "Stopped Needle Picture." After it was completed, the painting was extremely beautiful, and there were no traces of the seams. People from all over Shanghai came to see it. This painting was valued at three hundred taels of gold. Later, a wealthy merchant from Yangzhou brought a Han jade chain and a picture of a beauty by Zhou Fang to the Gu family, requesting an exchange, and took it away.

At that time, the name of Gu Embroidery was almost "a household name" throughout the country. Later, embroidery works in boudoirs were initially pretended to be from the Gu family, and then called imitations. Although it has now been lost, the name Gu Embroidery has become a very typical and popular name in the embroidery industry.

It was not until the county magistrate personally instructed the Public Security Bureau and dismissed patrol officers and leaders of the festival that the enthusiasm for the festival came to a halt. However, the people of Suzhou are still discussing the authorities' attitude towards the festival, which was lenient at first and strict later, as a topic of conversation after tea and dinner.
