Outline of Medical Construction (Part 1) 238

— Song Guobin

Over the years, the call for medical improvement has been loud. But do those who seek improvement have concrete methods? If we want the advancement of medicine, then everything that can help the development of medicine should be promoted and vigorously implemented, and everything that can hinder the development of medicine should be overthrown and eliminated. Today, our country's medicine is like a newly born seedling. It is not enough to nourish it with timely rain and fertilize it with manure to help it grow. It is not enough to remove its pests and cut down its weeds to fully develop it. Therefore, without considering my shallow knowledge, I have prepared an outline, which I call the Outline of Medical Construction.

(1) Medical Education: Those who dredge a stream must first treat the source. Those who plant a tree must first strengthen the base. Those who govern the world must first devote themselves to education. Why is medical construction any different? Therefore, I will first talk about medical education.

(A) Formulating Standards for Medical Curriculum and Improving Poor Medical Schools: Although there are 26 medical schools in the country, very few of their curricula can truly be called reasonable. The completeness or simplicity of the curriculum and equipment varies greatly. Therefore, the level of graduates also varies greatly. This is because of the uneven education they received, so they cannot achieve consistent results. Those who shoot must have a target before they know where to aim. Those who walk must have a direction before they know where to go. There has never been a case of effective governance and public compliance without a purpose or standard. Therefore, the formulation of standards for the medical curriculum is an urgent task. Now the government has an organization for the Medical Curriculum Standards Committee, and specific medical school curriculum standards are being drafted. This is what we are looking forward to and hoping will be implemented soon.

(B) Emphasizing Both Theory and Experience, Increasing Internship Time: The formulation of the medical education curriculum is as mentioned above. But what standards should be used? I say, equal emphasis on clinical medicine and basic medicine. Medicine is a practical science. It must have experimentation and practice. In domestic schools, there is generally more time spent reading in the classroom and less time spent practicing in the hospital. After graduation, students often have deep theoretical knowledge but insufficient experience when they start their practice. Even worse, they even use patients as experiments. This is a very dangerous thing. Now, if we increase the time spent practicing to three years or more, so that they already have rich experience during their student years, then they can handle things with ease when they start their practice, and there will be no cases of using patients as experiments.

(C) Adding a Course in Medical Ethics to Train Good Doctors: It is said that "if you are not a good minister, then be a good doctor." To call a doctor good is not only because of their superior knowledge, but also because of their noble character. This is why domestic medical schools must add a course in medical ethics. A doctor is a profession, and they have a special position with respect to the country, society, patients, and colleagues. The ethics they should follow cannot be fully covered by ordinary ethics. If they do not cultivate a good character during their studies, then it will be difficult to avoid unethical and unjust actions after they start their practice. In recent years, medical disputes have emerged one after another, and there has been much unethical competition among colleagues. This shows that doctors lack adequate self-discipline and proper conduct. If we can add a course in medical ethics to train good doctors, then in a few years, the so-called medical disputes will naturally decrease invisibly.

(D) Increasing the Number of Standard Medical Schools in Each Province to Increase the Production of Formal New Doctors: Recently, those who talk about medical education have the theory of emphasizing quality and emphasizing quantity. Those who emphasize quality advocate raising the level of medical education without necessarily establishing more medical schools. Those who emphasize quantity believe that the number of new doctors in the country is insufficient, and it is necessary to establish more medical schools to produce a large number of new doctors. I believe that the two theories can be used together and should not be abandoned partially. The fact that the number of new doctors in the country is insufficient is indeed true. And the desire to establish more medical schools to produce a large number of new doctors is an urgent task at the moment. However, in this regard, we must not only increase the number of medical schools, but also examine the content of the medical schools, ensuring that the schools added all meet the standards of the medical curriculum. Only then will those produced be formal new doctors. Otherwise, if we only seek quantity and do not ask about quality, and produce crudely and indiscriminately, with quack doctors everywhere, this is what Confucius meant by "What's the use of having many?"

(2) Medical Administration

Medical administration is a branch of government administration. Our country's medical administration has been neglected for a long time. There is no news of anything being done to promote benefits and eliminate harms to protect the development of our medical profession. Our medical community has also provided the government with policy guidelines and implementation materials. Why has the government not expressed anything? Now, I will repeat it without fear of being annoying.

One of the Common Summer Skin Diseases: Eczema (Part Two) 239

— Ji Jilin

The above six stages are what is commonly seen in eczema. However, its progression is not necessarily as complete as described. The progression varies depending on the strength of the cause, the speed of onset, the duration of the irritation, the individual's constitution, and the location of the occurrence. It may be cured during the erythema stage, or it may start as papules from the beginning. Some cases resolve after the vesicles and pustules dry and form scabs. There are also cases that proceed neatly from the first stage to the sixth stage. Now that the progression of eczema is clear, I will further describe its symptoms, broadly divided into two types: acute and chronic. In the initial stage of acute eczema, the skin becomes flushed, swollen, hot, and itchy, often accompanied by mild systemic symptoms such as chills. Children may even develop a fever. The affected area gradually transforms into papules and vesicles, then into pustules, forming crusts. After the crusts fall off, it becomes scaly and heals. However, if the underlying cause and all contributing factors are not addressed, the condition will inevitably recur, eventually becoming chronic eczema. Its stubbornness and difficulty to treat are even greater than in the acute stage, and the itching is also more severe. Excessive scratching often exacerbates the inflammation, leading to ulceration. Therefore, it is advisable to seek appropriate treatment during the acute stage of eczema.

Eczema commonly occurs on the head, face, hands, feet, neck, flexural surfaces of joints, groin, and breasts. The symptoms vary slightly depending on the location. Here is a brief description of a few:

(1) Eczema of the Head and Face: It usually starts with chills, followed by flushing and swelling of the face, and the appearance of small papules, vesicles, or pustules. It gradually spreads to the scalp and becomes chronic. However, it can also start on the scalp and then spread to the face. It is more common in children because their skin is thin and easily irritated by external factors.

(2) Eczema of the Hands and Feet: It may develop on the toes, forming a small number of vesicles, or it may invade the entire hand or foot, causing severe swelling and the formation of numerous vesicles. The itching is exceptionally intense. When it occurs on the lower legs, it is often associated with varicose veins, frequently causing thickening and edema of the skin.

(3) Eczema of the Genitals: It occurs on the scrotum, perineum, and other areas, appearing red and moist, with or without scaling. In severe cases, the entire area may become edematous, or it may spread to the surrounding area of the anus.

(4) Intertriginous Eczema: In obese individuals, it often occurs on the neck, between the thighs, and in areas such as the armpits, under the breasts, and flexural surfaces of joints. The skin is constantly rubbed against itself, and the irritation of sweat further promotes the development of eczema. It can also spread from the neck or breasts to the entire trunk.

Page 18

The treatment of eczema varies depending on the stage of its progression, the different symptoms, and the unpredictable changes. For example, in the erythema and papule stages, non-irritating dusting powders, alcoholic washes, and drying lotions are suitable. A single method or a combination of several methods may be used, depending on the doctor's experience. For instance, when the itching is unbearable, an alcoholic wash may be used first, followed by a dusting powder on the same area. In the vesicle and pustule stages, dusting powders or calamine lotion should be applied. During the weeping stage, areas not covered by crusts should be treated with wet compresses. For mild cases of weeping, dusting powders may also be used. When both weeping and crusting are severe, ointments should be applied and bandaged. The bandages should be changed frequently when there is a large amount of serous drainage. For facial eczema, where bandaging is inconvenient, adhesive plasters may be used. In the scaling stage, ointments such as white precipitate mercury ointment should be used. In general, although eczema is a common skin disease, the treatment should be based on a clear understanding of the nature of the therapy and the state of the eczema, selecting the appropriate treatment. For chronic and stubborn eczema, systemic therapy, such as injections and oral medications, may be necessary. It is crucial to seek guidance from a doctor before attempting any treatment rashly. For the patient's sake, attention should be paid to:

(1) Health Preservation: Avoid irritating foods and drinks (such as alcohol, vinegar, scallions, and ginger), and ensure regular bowel movements.

(2) Avoid External Irritation: Such as friction or pressure from clothing.

As for the treatment methods, consult a doctor. Otherwise, not only will the opportunity for treatment be missed, but there will also be unnecessary losses in terms of mental well-being, physical strength, and finances.

Common Sense Q&A on Diseases 240

— Cheng Hanzhang

(35) Appendicitis and Periappendicitis

(Q) What is the appendix?

(A) The appendix is a small, worm-like appendage that extends from the cecum, which is the beginning of the large intestine. It was formerly translated as the vermiform process. That is what it is.

(Q) What is the cecum?

(A) The cecum is the beginning of the large intestine, the sac-like portion that hangs down below where it connects to the small intestine, but it does not connect to the small intestine.

(Q) Are appendicitis and periappendicitis the same disease?

(A) Anatomically, they should be considered two separate diseases because the affected parts are different. However, they often occur simultaneously in clinical practice, and the symptoms are similar, making it difficult to distinguish between them. Therefore, they are usually discussed together.

(Q) What are the causes of this disease?

(A) There are only three possible causes. (1) The unique structure of the appendix, such as a narrow lumen, many folds in the mucosa, nutrient vessels that are end arteries, and an abundance of lymphoid tissue, are all factors that can induce the disease. (2) Constipation, the intrusion of fish bones or worms, or inflammation of the uterine adnexa are also contributing factors. (3) It can also be induced during the course of infectious diseases.

(Q) What are the initial symptoms of appendicitis and periappendicitis?

(A) They begin with acute abdominal pain, nausea (sometimes vomiting), and loss of appetite. There is a coated tongue, and constipation is common.

(Q) Are there any specific differences between this type of abdominal pain and ordinary abdominal pain?

(A) The abdominal pain that occurs during appendicitis is often widespread at first; within 24 hours, it becomes localized to the right lower abdomen. At the same time, there is tenderness in this area.

(Q) What external phenomena are present in the right lower abdomen?

(A) There is reflexive tension in the abdominal wall in the right lower abdomen; movement during breathing is less pronounced than on the left side. The abdominal wall reflexes are often absent.

(Q) Are there any abnormalities in the right leg?

(A) The right leg often assumes a flexed position.

(Q) Does the patient have a fever?

(A) A fever of 38 to 40 degrees Celsius is common; however, some patients do not have a fever.

(Q) What is the condition of the patient's pulse?

(A) Rapid; but in mild cases, it is less than 100 beats per minute. The faster the pulse rate, the more severe the condition.

(Q) How long does the course of this disease usually last?

(A) In mild cases, it can be cured in just a few days. There are also cases that recur later. Some may develop a periappendiceal abscess that ruptures spontaneously. If surgical removal is not performed, it may rupture naturally into the peritoneal cavity, intestines, bladder, etc. The most dangerous complications are septicemia or widespread perforating peritonitis, which are often fatal.

(Q) What should be the treatment principles for appendicitis and periappendicitis?

(A) During the acute phase, the patient should rest absolutely and abstain from food for one to two days. Milk, meat broth, egg yolk, and fruit juice can be given. Once the pain has subsided, a soft diet can be gradually introduced after a week. Sedatives are the main medications used; enemas are used to promote bowel movements. When it transitions to a chronic state, coarse foods should be avoided, bowel movements should be monitored, and warm, moist compresses or ichthammol ointment should be applied to the abdomen. In addition, surgical removal is best performed as early as possible, as the degree of danger increases with delay. In critical situations, surgery must be performed promptly.

Common Sense on Ear, Nose, Throat, and Eye Hygiene (Continued) 241

— Tang Renjin

(10) Hypertrophy of the Palatine Tonsils

Those who have read the ninth issue of this publication probably already understand what the tonsils are. Therefore, it will be much easier to discuss the pathological changes of the tonsils. The most important pathological changes of the tonsils are their proliferation and inflammation. The palatine tonsils are most susceptible to proliferation and hypertrophy. The pharyngeal tonsils are second. Now, I will first discuss hypertrophy of the palatine tonsils. In the next issue, I will discuss adenoid hypertrophy.

Hypertrophy of the palatine tonsils, originally named Hypertrophiatonsillaepalatiuae, seems to be more common in children in clinical practice. It is especially likely to occur in children with a scrofulous constitution. However, it also occurs in adults in no small numbers. This is because it is often induced by acute tonsillitis. This disease also has a genetic relationship. For example, if a child has this condition, their parents may also have had the same disease, or siblings may have the condition. We doctors often encounter these examples. In mild cases of this condition, there is no significant discomfort. Sometimes there is only an abnormal sensation in the throat. This is due to inflammation of the throat. In severe cases, the palatine tonsils are noticeably enlarged, even touching each other on both sides. The pharyngeal cavity is also narrowed as a result (see figure). Patients also complain of various symptoms, namely: (1) Narrowing of the throat, with an abnormal sensation. (2) Difficulty swallowing and breathing. (3) Inaccurate pronunciation. (4) Nasal snoring during sleep. (5) Reflex symptoms, such as coughing, wheezing, and headache. (6) The tonsillar crypts are mostly deep and wide, often with white or yellowish-white curd-like debris. This debris is medically known as tonsillar plugs (Mandelpfropf). Microscopic examination reveals dried secretions, desquamated epithelium, and various bacteria.

Children or adults with hypertrophy of the palatine tonsils are very susceptible to rhinitis, tonsillitis, otitis media, and tracheobronchitis. It can also be complicated by adenoid hypertrophy and acute or chronic rheumatic arthritis. Therefore, this condition has a great impact on human health. Regarding treatment, medication is ineffective. Surgery is required. However, in mild cases of hypertrophy, the tonsils may atrophy due to physiological regression during puberty. In that case, surgery is not necessary, and it can heal on its own (especially in children). If the hypertrophy is severe and has already caused narrowing of the pharyngeal cavity, difficulty swallowing and breathing, or frequent tonsillitis, then surgery is necessary. There are two surgical methods. One is called tonsillotomy, which is a method of removing part of the palatine tonsils. It is mostly used in children. The other is called tonsillectomy, which is a method of removing the entire palatine tonsils. It is mostly used in adults. However, the local conditions and the overall health must also be considered before deciding which surgical method to use. Fortunately, this decision is the responsibility of a specialist doctor, so you don't need to discuss it in detail.

The condition of hypertrophy of the palatine tonsils in the oral cavity is shown in the diagram on the left.

(4) Soft palate

(5) Uvula

(6) Anterior palatine arch

A Brief Discussion of Pulmonary Tuberculosis (16) 242

— Hu Jiayan

Chapter 6: Staging of Pulmonary Tuberculosis

It is almost universally known that pulmonary tuberculosis is divided into stages one, two, and three. The general public is probably aware that stage one is curable, stage two is somewhat different, and stage three is almost hopeless. This idea originated entirely from the theory of Turban Gerhardt. His main points are: (1) Stage one. At this stage, the affected area is very small. It is mild and limited to a small portion of a lobe of the lung, specifically at the apex of the lung and not exceeding the clavicle boundary. Fine rales may or may not be present upon auscultation. (2) Stage two. Now, it has spread outward from a small localized area, but in any case, it remains behind stage three. (3) Stage three. At this stage, one or several lobes are in a state of infiltration, and cavities have formed. This division into three stages is entirely based on the extent of the disease and is unrelated to the nature of the lesions in pathological anatomy. Therefore, its academic value is not very high. We must understand that there are no absolute boundaries to the progression and course of any disease; the most regular is true pneumonia. Its external symptoms and internal pathological anatomical changes almost correspond to each other like "a drum and its beat." However, its pattern of disease is not always so exemplary. It is even more difficult for pulmonary tuberculosis, which has the most complex disease course! Its clinical symptoms and course are not at all fixed, and in terms of pathological anatomy, although there are various distinctions between proliferative and exudative caseation and cavitation, the lungs of most patients contain almost all types. Based on this situation, it is almost impossible to divide pulmonary tuberculosis into stages in academic terms. This approach of relying on the area of the disease is, of course, a helpless measure, but it is clear, understandable, and easy to grasp. This classification has already been adopted in the statistical rules for the disease, and as a result, it has become universally known and regarded as a matter of course in the general public.

Each Person's Own Sky (Part Two) 243

— Huang Yiqing

The theater is the only venue where "people of all kinds" can "meet by chance," as the Buddha said, based on affinities. It is also a mysterious place where various communicable disease germs can "get their due" and spread. In other words, when opportunities are not good, the theater can become an infectious disease exchange, and the bulk of the traded goods are droplet-borne infectious diseases — most respiratory infectious diseases fall into this category. Although soldiers and police are hired at the door to provide protection, they can only prevent petty criminals from causing trouble or stop uninvited guests (perhaps distinguished guests who have complimentary tickets but forgot to bring them) from watching the show for free, but they cannot refuse patients and disease carriers from entering and buying tickets — because our country's reports of "statutory infectious diseases" and measures to isolate patients and disease carriers have not yet been implemented, there are particularly many mobile patients and disease carriers who frequent game venues. Since droplet-borne infectious diseases are inevitably mixed in the theater, these people each "blow their own trumpets" and spray droplets. At the same time, because there are many people and little air in the theater, people have to inhale the air exhaled by others for replenishment. Healthy tourists inevitably inhale the droplets of patients or disease carriers one after another. People with weak resistance become ill when they go home. When they are critically ill and on their deathbeds, they do not even know how they got infected, and they secretly lament in their hearts that they are "as hapless as Guan Yu and Zhang Fei." Is this not very sad!

In the theater, in order to obtain mental recreation, we sometimes inevitably contract droplet-borne infectious diseases in this way. Their deadly effects must be carried out "without the slightest deviation" and "settled on time." It is really not worth the loss and is not a good deal. Therefore, when there is a certain droplet-borne infectious disease in the area — such as influenza, whooping cough, pneumonia, measles, plague, as well as cerebrospinal meningitis, diphtheria, scarlet fever, etc. — it is best to temporarily stop going to the theater. If a famous actor, a famous blockbuster, or a famous artist comes along during this time, it would be a pity to miss them. If you have to bite the bullet and go see them, then it is best to act as an "ultra-modern monster" in a dignified manner and wear a face mask to watch the show without being polite. This is almost like "converting a beast into a child, with a chivalrous woman as a neighbor." If there is no way to subdue the "demon," then have a protective "talisman." This can allow hygiene to coexist with entertainment, and entertainment should not forget hygiene! In fact, in the future, if hygiene can be effectively implemented in various places, except when influenza is rampant, even if theaters are closed, it will be impossible to prevent other acute droplet-borne infectious diseases from spreading. At that time, the local health authorities may have to first order theaters to temporarily suspend business in order to prevent and control the diseases. When that happens, even if theatergoers and movie fans want to have a good time, they will not be able to.

As for the theater, if it knows its responsibilities and wants to make people entertain themselves and benefit from it, and not make people want to benefit but suffer losses, it should provide the best comfort facilities at any time for the limited ticket price. Everything from the smooth flow of air, appropriate temperature and humidity, and the suppression of dust, to the promotion of re-entry passes during breaks (theaters should also insert break times), should be strived for to be perfect. At the same time, attention should be paid to banning vendors, waiters, tea, teacups, and tidying up spittoons and toilets, so that everything is clean and can show that it is a high-class entertainment venue. That is the most beautiful merchant ethics; it really has a great impact on business. Bad theaters will be naturally sanctioned by society, even if local authorities do not crack down on them. As long as everyone has been burned once and has the prejudice of "never again," that theater will have no patrons in no time. In the future, when everyone pays attention to hygiene, this sanction will definitely be even fiercer than it is now! Moreover, many of these phenomena are unique to small cities in the mainland. In the countryside, when offering sacrifices to the gods, "grass stage troupes" are invited to perform in open-air sheds, just like open-air movies in the city in summer. The capacity and flow of air are not a problem. To be honest, if the lower-class theaters in the city are unable to improve, they might as well return to simplicity and start performing in the open air.

(Regarding the construction of public assembly halls, various cities in the interior of our country are still lacking. The hygiene points that should be noted during construction and management are the same as those for theaters before.)

Free Talk

Humor and Cynicism 244

— Hui

The East has a tradition of despotism. Turkey, Persia, and India, as a rule, both govern and are governed. Although this situation persists in the present world, no thinking person can deny the influence of social contract theory in the world.

As a rule, equality is sought, but inequality remains. The situation of inequality is unavoidable. At this time, thought usually has only one way out — cynicism. It is the salvation that the oppressed use to survive.

If one can live, can die, can laugh, can cry, and emotions each have appropriate development, the world is at peace. If one cannot seek to live, cannot seek to die, is not allowed to laugh, and is not allowed to cry, destroying emotions without remainder, then everything is chaotic. Whenever one is not allowed to cry or laugh, a liberation suddenly comes — that is humor, a kindred spirit of cynicism.

People's emotions are often timid in the face of truth and fear reality. They only watch tragic tragedies and only watch comedies that are boring. Therefore, a kind of comedy must come, concealing the truth and muddling through the time, giving people a kind of release. They laugh loudly and disperse. Just seeing that people who are good at telling jokes are welcomed by everyone in society knows this principle.

Humor and cynicism are also different. The latter has meaning, the former has no meaning. The latter belongs to the protagonist of the play, the former belongs to the clown. The two are both hard workers. For example, deliberately making people laugh and making all kinds of strange shapes also requires painstaking management.

Conversely, the governed are cynical, and those who govern are humorous. Under a despotic tyrant, if one wants to offer advice obliquely, one must take a roundabout route. A belly full of jokes and various strange shapes is indispensable. This is no less than the功勞 of other "royal assistants." Only Qu Yuan was too serious, "Will he use the sudden and slippery humor as grease or leather to clean the pillars and level the ground?" He has already included humorists in the oil category. This is enough to show Qu Yuan's cynicism.

But there are some other questions: Does China only have comedies, or does it also have tragicomedies? Is it deliberately pretending to be ugly feet, or is the ugly foot pretending to be a lead actor? Is it somewhere between an ugly foot and a non-ugly foot, or is it playing some ancient drama for people to watch three thousand years ago? …

Impressions of Zibo 245

— Luo Wang

(9) A Visit to the North and South Pavilions

Stealing leisure in a busy schedule, we made a trip to the North and South Pavilions one early morning.

Leaving Boshan Gate and crossing the bridge, we arrived at the North and South Pavilions, famous for their scenery. First we went to the North Pavilion, formerly Yiyuan, now Yiyuan Elementary School. There is a Thunder God Temple, and the incense is still strong. There is a pavilion facing the goldfish pond. On the wall is engraved the four characters "Kites Flying and Fish Leaping," which have a magnificent air. There are very large goldfish in the pond, but it is a pity that the pond water is not clear and there is not much elegance.

Leaving the North Pavilion, we crossed the street to the South Pavilion. It is now the site of the Construction Bureau and is said to be the place where Fan Zhongyan lived. There is a spring inside, the pond is about one square zhang, and the locals named it Fan Spring because of this. A temple was built and called Fan Gong Temple.

However, we have been to Changshan, and it is true that Fan Zhongyan grew up in Changshan; moreover, Boshan was not a large county in the past, so why would Fan Gong come here? The local legends are really a bit unreliable.

The Fan Spring leaves the South Pavilion and divides into three streams flowing outward, south to Qianyuan and north to Yiyuan; the other stream flows west along the stone bridge into the city. This stream of spring water is very interesting. This is really a unique spectacle of Boshan!

On the Future of Graduates and the "Quota System" for Admissions 246

— Xiao Mo

The plight of intellectuals as commodities is a universally lamented issue, both ancient and modern. From the Master Confucius, who "waited for a good price to sell himself," to graduates who use diplomas as trademarks, all prove that the value of intellectuals is not much higher than that of slaves in ancient Eastern markets. With the commodification of labor, knowledge itself has gained exchange value, and intellectuals have become owners of a special commodity. However, due to the lack of progress in Chinese society, intellectuals are not yet able to speak of free contracts; even those who study "science" cannot avoid selling themselves.

The difference between the use value of intellectuals and the use value of manual laborers is like the difference between hunting dogs and oxen in the eyes of their master. However, this commodity of all living beings is, after all, somewhat different from other commodities. When wheat or coffee cannot be sold, they can only be stored in warehouses to rot. But scholars who cannot find enlightened masters to serve will lament, feel isolated and indignant, or even take risks. Although a failed scholar's rebellion takes three years to materialize, if the sighing farmers on the loess plateau are incited, the world will become troubled from then on. This is why the examination system, which resembles a commodity exposition and a commodity inspection bureau, is so valuable!

In today's economic panic, it is not only general commodities that are overproduced, but also this special commodity – the commodity of knowledge – is inevitably overproduced as well. On the one hand, there is "social dumping." On the other hand, this commodity, lacking an outlet for absorption, collapses and overflows, and political extremism emerges. The situation in China is even more tragic. Every year, special factories – schools – produce them in batches with crude and shoddy workmanship and push them onto the market. However, supply exceeds demand, and sales are sluggish. As long as this phenomenon exists, society will not be stable. Therefore, this matter must be given attention.

As the summer vacation approaches each year, newspapers often feature articles about sending off graduates or discussing the future of students. This year is even more lively, and among them, the most noteworthy is Dr. Hu Shih's article "A Gift to This Year's University Graduates" (Wen, 24, Ta Kung Pao). In addition to three old self-defense prescriptions, he added a new one: "You must first reflect on yourself; do not blame others exclusively, and even less blame society." According to his high opinion, the reason why graduates cannot find a bowl of rice to eat is not because society does not need them, but because their own studies are not good, or they mistakenly entered a bogus school. What beautiful and sarcastic words! This is as if the commodities of a monopoly or large factory are saying to the commodities of small factories: "Do not complain about buyers or envy others; first, blame yourselves, who called your goods inferior and the brand of the factory you came from not old enough?" All unsold commodities, remember the lesson of the commodities from the famous and old brand Made in U.S.A.!

Recently, university graduates in Beiping have even formed an organization called the "Professional Sports League." Although there are no words like "civil rights" or "anti-imperialism," the terms "sports" and "league" are always jarring and could easily cause trouble. For the sake of stabilizing the political market, we should think of a control method.

We know that the most common way to alleviate overproduction is to limit production and stipulate the amount of commodity consumption – which is called the "quota system" in Japan and the "Quota System" in Europe and the United States. This method has been applied to the production of special commodity students in Hitler's Germany. As soon as Hitler came to power, he promulgated a law "Suppressing Overcrowding in German Schools" and adopted an admissions "quota system." But at that time, only Jewish students were restricted. By the end of last year, Germany had a new law restricting the number of university students in general. According to this law, the number of high school graduates who passed the university entrance exam and entered university in 1934 was limited to 15,000. But according to the government's estimate, there should be 27,600 male and 10,400 female students graduating from high school that year who could enter university. That is to say, three-fifths of the students who could have entered university were deprived of this right. This is not surprising. Before Hitler's dictatorship was established, the stagnation of the commodity of knowledge in Germany was already considerable: among 8,000 engineering graduates, only 1,000 found jobs; among 22,000 probationary teachers, only 3,900 obtained assistant teacher positions; and 72% of artists in Berlin had a monthly income of less than 50 marks. Under these circumstances, the increase in university students would naturally only spread more seeds for liberalism and extremism. Therefore, Hitler's restriction of the production of this special commodity is indeed a fundamental solution. It is unknown what China's control will be like in the future.

The Seizure of Occupations 247

— Cha Shiji

Recently, I read two articles in this publication on the issue of youth employment. One is by Mr. You Mo, and the other is by Mr. Bai Ge. The two men's opinions are completely opposite; Mr. You said that whether young people can find employment is definitely not because society does not have jobs to provide for them, but because there are no good jobs that young people idealize for them; Mr. Bai, on the other hand, believes that it is an overall social problem, meaning that there are simply not that many positions in society to supply new graduates.

Of the two views, I am naturally in agreement with Mr. Bai Ge. The reason is very simple, as Mr. Bai Ge said, "...even if young students in general follow the path pointed out by Mr. You, the result will only be to squeeze out another part of the employed people who have less opportunity to receive education and have not obtained a higher position, turning them into unemployed people, and exchanging their positions with each other."

The fundamental remedy for unemployment naturally lies in increasing the number of jobs, definitely not in exchanging them with each other. However, in this time of recession that pervades the world, what new development is possible? It is like a cup of water; when there are few thirsty people, everyone can be casual, but once there are many thirsty people and the amount is insufficient, a scramble will occur. The so-called scramble is just to "exchange" the owner of the job, that is, one of the unemployed gets a job, which means that an unemployed person is produced among the employed.

Silently observing the trend of current society, the job-grabbing movement is becoming increasingly blatant. Logically, the more competitors there are for jobs, the most talented should be employed, and the old and incompetent must be eliminated. The employer must feel the convenience of choice. But in reality, it is the exact opposite. When society is shrouded in profound panic, the struggle for survival is fierce, and the criteria for employing people will become more severe and narrow. The so-called severe is not the so-called assessment of talent, but "vested interests." In Chinese society, where feudal ideas are still deeply rooted, it will undoubtedly become pure kinship or localism. Those who do not have reliable fellow villagers and relatives will have greater difficulty finding employment than in more prosperous times.

Furthermore, from the perspective of those in employment, because of the large number of competitors, they must be cautious and work to preserve their current position. Like the customs and post office, where the number of people is relatively large, they have already formed very strong groups because of the examination relationship. Today, even those with fewer people have a considerable combination to deal with others' job grabbing. Therefore, the more depressed the times are, the more developed this kind of exclusive organization will be. Economically speaking, it seems to be a return from a free exchange economy to an ancient closed economy. In short, those who have already obtained employment are determined not to lose their position casually, so new graduates and young people will feel it more and more difficult to find a job.

From the above two reasons, we can know that even if the exchange of occupations (such as university students doing the work of middle school graduates, and middle school graduates doing the work of primary school graduates) can muddle through for a while, when the degree of panic is truly deepened, it will also be impossible even to exchange because employers are bound by vested interests and the employed are united in resistance.

In Defense of Literature 248

— Li Jinming

Mr. Wu Zhihui said in the "Free Talk" on August 1st: "Literature will not die, and the great disaster will not stop." These words are quite alarming.

Opening up the history of the East and West, from ancient times to the present, it seems that there has never been a literary writer who held a pen in one hand and a knife in the other. There has never been anyone who said that he used literature as a political program, sharpened his weapons and troops, attacked cities and expanded territories, and opposed the imperial dynasty. The Book of Songs was only the mournful voice of small people who were so weak that they did not even dare to speak. The composition of the Songs of Chu was only due to Qu Yuan's integrity and poverty and his inability to scheme and exploit. If it is said that he was actually jilted by a woman and deliberately made an issue of it, it is not impossible. As for the rebellious figures who were stimulated by the Book of Songs and the Songs of Chu later, there were absolutely none. To give a simple example: why did the author of the Water Margin not write Song Jiang and Wu Yong as ambitious men who "buried their heads in books" and "slapped the table and threw away their pens"? If it is said that the scattered poems such as "The old man with a broken arm from Xinfeng" and "Meat and wine rot within the red gate, while corpses freeze on the road" would arouse the heroic spirit of the Timely Rain, I am afraid that Shi Naian would not be able to give a concrete answer. Also, as for the wicked thieves Li Zicheng and Zhang Xianzhong, historical records and legends do not mention that they were "...generous, liked to help the helpless, and kept the Water Margin in their hands all day long, identifying themselves with Song Gongming..." etc. For example, what do Zhu De and Mao Zedong, etc., know about Habtermann, Suttermann, Wassermann, Henry Mann, and Thomas Mann? I am afraid they do not even understand what "literature" and what "mass language" are. ... Frankly speaking, not to mention in the junior high school history of our country, even in the Twenty-Four Histories, you can't find such an example.

Thinking about it in foreign countries, there is only one big rogue, Wei Long; but most of Wei Long's blind mess comes from legends and cannot be fully believed. As for Rousseau's influence on the French Revolution, it is also nonsense; in the era of Louis XVI in France, the people of Paris were in great chaos, and the number of refugees was increasing day by day. It was inevitable for them to rob bread, but Danton and Robespierre were some fierce figures, which goes without saying, but it has not been heard that these people talked about the philosophy of Diderot and Rousseau. Speaking of the demise of the Russian imperial family, frankly speaking, it has little to do with Tolstoy, Dostoevsky, or Gorky; if they did not suffer a defeat in the Far East and another defeat in Germany, they would not have collapsed so quickly. In short, no matter what form a country's politics takes, as long as it makes the masses have food to eat and everyone has nothing to say, and militarily it does not fail due to recklessness, endangering the country, even if writers come out and say a few irrelevant gossips, everyone will still find it annoying.

Old Man (2) 249

— Jin Yi

So they drank a lot of wine, and some people simply opened their throats and poured it down. (In fact, this cannot be considered a suitable reason, because their love for wine has always been well known.) Even those who do not have much money to buy a drunk (maybe even hungry for two meals) have to pretend to be tipsy, walk unsteadily, and deliberately speak vaguely. This is entirely for the sake of face.

Old Aksonov sat silently among his goods, squinting his eyes, half-sleeping and half-lying in the high-backed armchair. His red face, covered with wrinkles, was like an apple that had been exposed to the sun for three days, making people feel uncomfortable to look at. Moreover, he was dry and small, like a monkey, just lacking that sharp look. His eyes were not only not sharp, but always looked tired. No wonder, he had used them to look at the human world for seventy-four years. His hands were like chicken feet, with only a layer of skin wrapped around the bones, and the tendons were all sticking out.

Everyone who saw him felt even more terrified of old age. They asked themselves in their hearts: "Do I have to live to such a disgusting age?"

As for his goods, there were many kinds, with only one thing in common, and that was that they were old. Since it was an "old miscellaneous goods" shop, the oldness of the goods was natural, but the age of his goods was like that of his person, to the point where people could only sigh. Those goods included the most fashionable women's shawls in 1880, which had fifty years of history but had faded in color; there were also long leather boots with worn-off skin, old formal clothes and hats with countless holes eaten by insects, a gramophone that was made in the year it was invented, ironware that had turned yellow, a writing desk with one leg missing, many different things, some of which had never been seen by young people, and besides being surprised, they were also a little confused about their purpose.

Conversations

Ramblings on Social Climbing 250

— Ruo Wang

Dealing with the world requires an art, which no one denies anymore. However, there are all kinds of things in the world, so the art of dealing with the world is also very diverse. For example, if something needs to be scolded, then there is the "art of scolding people"; if it needs to be praised, there is also the "art of praising"; and love between men and women is even a most authentic art. If we were to discuss these categories separately, we could write a booklet priced at more than sixty cents, to say the least. If there is extra time, it is also possible to expand it into a monograph, but these are not something that little nobodies like us, who are respectfully called "contributors," are qualified to talk about, so let's stop here and get back to the main topic.

It is said that in the ancient palace-style high-rise building of the YMCA in Eight Immortals Bridge, a grand banquet began, with green lights and red wine – note: it is advisable to install green electric lights and drink red wine in summer – and white-collared guests filled the seats. If you, a little nobody, are also fortunately invited to attend, and it happens that you take the time to come, then you must not show the impatience of someone who has never eaten a big meal in your life, driving fast and gobbling up food. You must restrain your hunger a little and appear nonchalant, and even tell the waiter to say, "Today's steak is not as fresh as yesterday's." Or, after eating two bites, put it down and not eat it. In this way, others will think that you have eaten foreign bread abroad for several years, or at least they will always think that you are an old customer of the YMCA and dare not despise you.

So, is it over when you eat everything one by one? Of course not. So, what else do you do at the table? It all depends on your artistic skills and the situation at the time. If you feel the air is quiet, you can turn your mind two or three hundred times and find three or five jokes to tell, causing everyone at the table to spit out food and burst into laughter. The source of these jokes is best found among gentlemanly humorists, because this will show that you are also quite gentlemanly. But if you do not have any gentlemanly jokes to tell, you can also find another kind, but the people mentioned should still be found in high places, such as Hu Shih being caught visiting prostitutes in Beiping by his wife with bound feet, or Wu Zhihui running out of money on a boat and having to take off his gown and pawn it to the boatman.

If the air is mild and you need to talk about something a little more serious, then you see a friend of a certain writer, × someone, is also present, you can loudly ask, "Have you seen so-and-so these days?" If the answer is "No," then you immediately say, "If you see him, tell him that I have been a little uncomfortable these days and have rarely gone out." In this way, regardless of whether you know the writer or not, as long as you directly call him by his name, people will already know that you and the writer are old friends. And the matter of calling people by their names is really worth talking about.

If you call Zhang Xueliang the Young Marshal Zhang and Cai Yuanpei Cai Jiemin, people will guess that you have been a secretary.

Dropping a surname from a famous person's name, such as Dafu, Ziping, Fangwu, although people may not necessarily regard you as a celebrity, at least they will think that you are a friend of the celebrity. However, for celebrities who have no surname or whose surname is waived, you must add a surname to show that you are familiar with them, such as Bing Xin, call her Xie Bingxin, and Lu Yin, call her Huang Luyin.

If a friend has just been introduced to you, you will naturally ask him where he is from first. If he is from Nantong, you can casually say a person's name and ask, "Do you know someone named Zhang Jian in Nantong City?" Then you can talk about each other's academic interests. If the other person is studying art, you can talk about Liu Haisu, Xu Beihong, Lin Fengmian, etc. On the Western side, you can say a bunch of French names. If the other person is studying literature, then the material is even easier to pick up. If you feel that the conversation is empty, in the past few years you could have specially translated a little of the literary news translated by Zhao Jingshen and Yang Changxi as conversation material. Now you can also often look at the warrior literature on the butt of each newspaper to find out what lawsuit is being fought now.

If the other person likes to watch movies and talk about women, then you really can't finish talking for three days and three nights, so I have to put down the pen and not talk about it.

Old Zhong 251

— Ye Fei

Old Zhong is the oldest of our four colleagues. His surname is Zhong, and his mother named him Ah Gou. Later, when he entered school, the teacher gave him a more elegant name, called "Zuoting." Of course, this contains feudal ideas. His teacher came from the imperial examination, so he never forgot the well-known maxims that a scholar should have: "Studying is about the sages, and being an official is about the emperor and the country." "Zuoting" naturally hoped that he would be an official in the future and "assist the imperial court." Unfortunately, by the time he wanted to take the exam, the imperial examination had been abolished. Therefore, Old Zhong's dream of becoming an official finally had no "chance" to be realized, which is the most regrettable thing in his life!

However, people do not call him "Zuoting," but directly call him Old Zhong. These two words, Old Zhong, seem to be a very glorious title to him over the years, so when he meets people who call him Old Zhong, he is very proud. When talking to people, he often pats his chest with his left hand, raises his thumb with his right hand, points at his nose, and says:

"Hey! I, Old Zhong, am not bragging..." As he said this, he laughed triumphantly. The people listening to him also laughed so hard that they could not close their mouths.

Old Zhong's age is neither young nor old. He looks about forty years old. He himself has not counted it accurately. How old is he? We can only look at his face from the form. There is a saying in the countryside: "Don't ask the mother-in-law's age, but look at the mother-in-law's face." My answer also comes from looking at Old Zhong's face.

Although he is already in his forties, his chin is still so bald, like an old woman's face, unable to find a single whisker. It is not that he has the art of preserving his youth, but that every day as soon as he is free, he sits on a stool, takes a mirror, takes a pair of pliers, and clips it carefully, not stopping until there is not a single one left. Although he likes people to call him Old Zhong, he does not want people to say that he is old. If someone accidentally says that he is old, he will be unhappy; even, he will say with a strong tone of argument:

"Old! Who said that? You can only be considered old when you have a beard."

He has a wife, who also lives in Shanghai. She is a middle-aged woman who still has charm. Her relationship with him is not very good. She dresses up all day long and mixes in the amusement park. Her face is not very annoying, and her means of attracting bees and butterflies are even stronger, so

Page 22

She has a good record of mixing. She also had two children, a boy and a girl, but because they were not properly raised, they both died early.

Old Zhong has been a clerk in our store for a full three years. He is very friendly among his colleagues, and people also treat him as a child. Even if someone scolds him or says a few words to him, he just laughs it off and does not get angry. He only goes home for one night each year, going back on the night of the winter solstice and returning to the store early the next morning. Friends who like to joke always dig at him a few words.

"Old Zhong! You haven't been home for a long time. Your wife has eloped with a gigolo!"

"I don't care, I don't care. Who has time to answer them?"

"Haha! Great amount! Old Zhong! Touch your vest and see, ha! ha! ha!" A burst of wild laughter and applause made two red clouds fly to Old Zhong's face. Finally, he walked away mumbling and avoided their embarrassing teasing.

According to what he told us himself: when he was twenty-three or four years old, he also played a romantic comedy once. Later, the little girl did not know why she changed her mind and fell in love with another young man. He had no ability to take a young girl's heart back from someone else's hand. All he had was melancholy and disappointment!

Unfortunately, he said this story briefly and not in detail, so there is no way to write it down; otherwise, it would be a good material for the biography of Old Zhong.

In the Fiery Pit 252

— Especially

The hour hand pointed to the intersecting midnight line, pushing open the only window in that attic room. The empty sky was so dark, no moonlight, no starlight to be seen at all. Even the Milky Way stretching across was nowhere to be found. A silence prevailed, seemingly pregnant with rain.

Naturally, in this remote place, the streets would not be bustling. The lamps, like a string of bright pearls, swayed with a strangely quiet leisure. Occasionally, one or two pedestrians passed by, walking slowly and deliberately.

Inadvertently, a wail was carried over.

| Don't hit me anymore, ah... I won't dare again...

The voice was very soft and tender, like that of a child. In that somber weather, how sorrowful it must be! Indeed, the tone of the wailing gradually grew louder and louder. The voice was so familiar. I realized that it was the neighbor's little Bao again, experiencing corporal punishment.

Sitting on a stool near the window, for some reason, countless sparks were flashing before my eyes. Suddenly, the sparks separated, and it was |

...Brown hair, a diminutive body, a mismatched face, tattered clothing, and sallow, emaciated skin, swollen and throbbing eyeballs! No, not just these, but terror, fear... depicting an extremely complex outline.

| Clap, clap, clap... In the stillness, the clear sound of footsteps entered my ears.

| Hmph, you're still slacking off. Be careful...

The tone must have been very angry, which could be discerned from the intonation.

Indeed, crying was only an echo under ordinary beatings. If the torture was intensified, this echo would have to be suppressed. So, what was being broadcast here? Hastened scolding and reprimands!

When the sun was setting the next day, I came back from the street and entered the alley, carefully looking around. But where was little Bao? Gone, gone.

Truly, I didn't understand why I was so concerned about her. A sense of longing filled my chest. Yes, perhaps she was seriously injured? Perhaps she was lying in bed? Or perhaps she couldn't even move? Maybe... various thoughts were swirling around, without stopping.

At night, I tossed and turned in bed, my imagination running wild like a movie. Suddenly, a girl emerged, her flesh so emaciated, her upper body naked, covered with streaks of blood. Her eyes were filled with tears, and her lips were constantly sobbing. The tragic state on her face!

Finally, she cried, the corners of her mouth twitching, trembling, uttering low, faint moans!

| Heaven, when will I be able to escape this raging fiery pit?

When the breeze passed, it carried some lingering fishy smell. Emotions were in turmoil, and there was no way to calm them down. I raised my head. The rain outside the window was falling patteringly, wetting the desk, wetting the window, strangely desolate, as if symbolizing the fate of little Bao.

Deep Night Sorrow 253

— Zhen

The night is deep!

Everything is sinking into the lonely and desolate embrace of the night. The starlight has not flooded the azure sky. Coolness and darkness entwine the earth. The rustling of fallen leaves and the barking of dogs form the song of the night!

Gloom and coldness pervade the space. The earth is covered with a layer of gray gauze. Melancholy and indignation clog the chest. Pitiful! Dreams are again deeply knocking on my empty heart.

I seem to have knocked on every door of life, but every door is covered with the blood of innocent victims. I curse, I resent, I stare blankly at the crowd with a foolish smile. I curse these animals called humans, not knowing what monsters they are. They harm each other, they contradict each other, completely obliterating all that is truly "joy" and "suffering." Selfishness is displayed to the masses. Tightly embracing everyone's pathetic ambitions. Haha! In this ambition, trying to find "love" and "joy." How foolish! How pitiful!

The earth is still gloomy and dark. My whole body has a strong spasm. I swear that those who build their own happiness on the suffering of others should perish. Sadness and pain are intertwined in my chest. This long, long night has no dawn. The heavens and earth are still covered with a layer of dim haze.

Eating Melons Is Not the Melon Planter 254

Amateur Mailbox

Changing Careers Is Painful 255

— Editor

My respected Editor:

I am nineteen years old this year. In the first month of my fourteenth year, my family sent me to work as an apprentice in the largest silk and cloth store in the neighboring county. It has been six years now. I don't know what I've learned in these six years. I always feel very bored and I'm afraid that there will be no hope in the future, so I want to change to work as a trainee in a bank. Because I think that if I enter a bank, I will definitely have time to handle matters and be able to study in the evenings, which will increase my knowledge. If I continue to waste my time in a cloth store, I asked my father to find a trainee position for me in a bank in July of this year, but it was not easy to find one for a while. I thought that rather than entering a bank as a trainee, I should leave the store early and make up for some academic subjects so that it would be more convenient for me to serve in the future. So I asked my father to let me go to Shanghai first to enter a vocational school to study business subjects. He agreed, so I gave up my six years of learning on July 20 and went to Shanghai. Now I live with relatives. When I arrived in Shanghai, I took the entrance exam for a vocational school. I took the first-year junior-level exam with an elementary school diploma. Fortunately, I managed to get into a vocational school. However, when my father heard that I had arrived in Shanghai, he immediately wrote a letter saying: "Since you have been studying commerce for six years, it is not convenient to go back to school. In my opinion, it is better to open a national goods store yourself. What do you think?" I had thought of this earlier, but because there is already a national goods company organization in the area and the market is sluggish, it is not easy to open a store. So I replied that I did not agree. But! I am now feeling "the infinite pain of changing careers!" Because if I go to school now and study from the first year of junior high school, I will be twenty-five years old when I graduate from high school. And my father cannot allow it. This is impossible in reality. If I study business for one or two years, I don't know if there will be a bank job for me after these one or two years. If I don't go to school, I can't go back, because I have already resigned as a shop assistant, and I swore when I was in the shop that I would not go back. If you ask me to go back, I will only jump into the Huangpu River! So these days, after thinking back and forth, I feel that the future is dark and terrible! For my own sake, I am determined not to work hard towards that bright road, so I presumptuously and urgently ask Mr. to indicate the needle of the south. I am infinitely grateful. The weather is very hot, and the writing is very rough. Please forgive me. I wish you

Safety 何士聰

Answer: I think your problem is not difficult to solve. You can temporarily study at the school, but on the other hand, you must quickly look for a job. If you don't want to be a clerk in an old-fashioned store anymore, ask someone to find you a position as a bank trainee or other position you want to do. Nowadays, there are no strict regulations on academic qualifications for banks to recruit trainees or junior staff. The main thing is to look at the results of the exam. And the exam seems to focus on work experience. Therefore, what you should pay attention to is to work hard to train your business skills and learn work skills. You don't necessarily have to graduate from school.

Secondly, from the perspective of learning, you don't necessarily have to go to school. Most of the real skills are experienced in actual life. Moreover, as long as you are determined to learn, you can also study book knowledge on your own. You don't necessarily have to "have a teacher to teach you." The only good thing about school compared to self-study is that you have one more diploma, which is not a guarantee. It cannot guarantee you a job. Therefore, there are many, many people who cannot find a job even after graduating from business school. School is not a job placement agency either.

In addition, I have two additional points of advice to give you: First, being a shop assistant now is certainly hopeless, but being a clerk in a new-style company or foreign firm is not much better. Therefore, you don't have to always "see that the mountain is higher than this one" and try to change careers. Second, you certainly need work skills to do things, but in this contradictory society, unemployment is very common. Even if you have the skills, you may not necessarily have a job. But you need to live, and think that life cannot be improved from now on, and the job will never be guaranteed. There are ways. As long as you recognize the social contradictions and the crux of the job problem, you will naturally know how you should work hard.

Novel

The Idiot (5) 256

— Lin Bin

The idiot was silent, and tears rolled from the corners of his eyes onto his cheeks. But then he burst into a frantic song of vulgar and lewd mountain tunes, as if venting the infinite boredom in his chest.

Time passed day by day, and the long winter finally came to an end. The warm spring sun洒滿滿 the earth, like the smile of a holy maiden. Nature was covered with a brilliant new outfit, showing off the alluring coquettishness of a seductive slut, scattering an intoxicating and stifling warmth. The mysterious fire of youth was burning in every cell of every young man and woman, causing mysterious changes in their bodies and souls, increasing the happiness of the lucky and the sorrow of the unfortunate.

Just as the few apple-colored faces symbolizing countless common people were floating with smug smiles, dreaming rosy dreams, our long-term worker, who was eating for free without pay, was like a traveler who had been thirsty for a long time in the desert drinking poison, and was immediately dominated by an excitement that led to the path of death, causing him to forget the fear that an idiot should have, and forget the danger and death.

One night, the idiot's neighbor suddenly heard the chickens in her chicken coop screaming loudly, thinking that a tabby cat was dragging a chicken. She一边一边, lit a kerosene lamp, put on her clothes, opened the door, and rushed to the chicken coop to shine a light. One of the oldest hens that laid the most eggs was gone. She was as heartbroken as if she had lost her beloved son, and could not close her eyes all night.

The next day, just as dawn was breaking, before the idiot had gotten up, the housewife who had lost her chicken walked out of the bedroom door. Her eyes still had the shadows of tears from last night, and she searched every corner for signs of the hen being harmed. Suddenly, she saw the lost hen rushing out of the corner of the cattle pen where the idiot was staying, as if in a dream, and was startled. She immediately took a handful of rice and scattered it on the ground, coaxing it to come closer. She grabbed it in her arms like a treasure. The warm body of the chicken clearly spent the night in the quilt.

Like a toy that children were tired of playing with, the idiot once again gained people's surprised gaze and fierce laughter.

A few days later, a shocking news spread throughout the village. The news first came from the mouths of several cowherds, and then it spread throughout the village like wildfire. The women whispered to each other, as if someone's young cousin had secretly given birth to a child. The old women hummed "Amitabha" one after another, as if trying to use this "Amitabha" to resolve infinite sins. Some nosy men even specially composed a little song that was unbearable to the ears, and the children recited it to each other. The news was:

"The idiot is having an affair with the nun of the Auspicious Nunnery."

Speaking of the nun of this Auspicious Nunnery, she is also really pitiful. She was born in a farming family, and she had her fortune told twice since she was a child, and both times it was said that she would kill three husbands. When she was nine years old, she had smallpox, and her face was as pockmarked as the lid of a copper fire bucket, and she had the nickname "Full of Stars." So the pitiful girl's fate as a nun was naturally destined. She entered our Auspicious Nunnery when she was twelve years old, and it has been more than ten years now. Last year, she lost her old master, and now she is the only abbot of this nunnery.
